Current Affairs Commentary

The Meeting of Italy, Austria, and Hungary and Peace in Central Europe

At the time of the meeting of Italy, Austria, and Hungary in Rome, foreign telegrams have been received that the situation in Central Europe seems to be increasingly complex. Not only the rumors of Austria's restoration and the news of Germany and the Little Entente's preparations for war are rampant, but also the claims that Italy is increasing troops in the north and colluding with the Little Entente, that Hitler is sharpening his sword and approaching Yugoslavia, are also being discussed. Whether the meeting of Italy, Austria, and Hungary is an economic meeting or not is a matter of debate. If this intricate and deceitful situation will lead to a second world war, whether the Little Entente will eventually lean towards Germany or resolutely join hands with Italy, or still rely on France, whether Italy's actions can be ignored by Britain and France, or will cause greater turbulence, are all issues that deserve attention.

However, by synthesizing the facts and weighing the current situation, we know that although the situation in Central Europe is very tense, it has not yet reached the point of a major war. The contradictions between the countries of Central Europe were caused by the peace treaty after the war. Since the signing of the treaty, the tense situation between the countries has been seen many times, but they have all been able to return to calm. This is because the disaster of war is too great, so they all dare not be the first to start a war easily. However, if these treaties are not revised one day, the opportunity for war in Europe will inevitably not be cut off for one day. If the opportunity for war is not cut off, there will inevitably be a day when it breaks out. Once it breaks out, it will be a major war, and the countries of Europe will inevitably suffer both losses. Taking today as an example, if Germany decides to invade Austria, war will inevitably break out. If Austria is restored, war cannot be avoided. If the combination of Italy, Austria, and Hungary is political rather than just economic, then war is even more unavoidable.

In short, if any of these occur, war can break out. If Germany invades Austria, it will be enough to threaten Italy and will be particularly detrimental to Czechoslovakia. Therefore, Italy and Czechoslovakia will inevitably participate in the war. At this time, the war will become a war between Germany and Austria, Italy, and Czechoslovakia. If Austria is restored, although it will be beneficial to Italy, it will be particularly detrimental to Hitler's Germany and the Little Entente. Therefore, Germany and the Little Entente will inevitably act simultaneously and approach Austria. At this time, Austria, Hungary, and Italy will be one group, and Germany and the Little Entente may be another group. Hitler's opposition to the restoration of Austria-Hungary is probably because his desire to merge Austria and build a "Third Reich" cannot be realized. The reason why the Little Entente opposes the restoration of Austria-Hungary is that most of the land of the Little Entente is the former territory of the Austro-Hungarian Empire before the war, and the various ethnic groups of the Little Entente have suffered the pain of being enslaved and ruled by the Habsburg imperial family. If the restoration is successful, then Austria-Hungary, which has been thinking about getting rid of the shackles of the treaty, will take advantage of Italy's assistance and prepare to restore its lost land. Therefore, the fear of recovery is more intense than that of Germany. This can be confirmed by past facts without any doubt. For example, on March 27, 1921, when Charles of the Habsburg imperial family came to Hungary to usurp the throne, Czechoslovakia, Romania, and Yugoslavia coordinated their troops to invade Hungary. Within three weeks, Charles fled again. The political and economic alliance of the Little Entente was also founded at this time. The Little Entente Convention was concluded in February last year. The combination of these three countries is a further step. The most notable is the coordination of the three countries' diplomacy and economic cooperation, which is almost the same as one country. All of this is prompted by the concern about the restoration of Austria-Hungary. Therefore, Austria-Hungary will not be restored today. If it is restored, the attack of the Little Entente will inevitably precede that of Germany. If so, then Italy and Germany will be difficult to sit idly by. Therefore, if Austria is restored, war cannot be avoided. But can war be avoided if Austria is not restored? This depends on whether the nature of today's meeting between Italy, Austria, and Hungary is economic or political. If it is economic, then it is just to find an economic outlet for Austria and Hungary, which can be tolerated by all parties. If it is political, then it has the suspicion of changing the current territory of Central Europe and will inevitably cause the resistance of the Little Entente and will also lead to the intervention of France and Britain. Therefore, if Mussolini acts arbitrarily, it will also be enough to cause war to break out.

However, judging from the current situation, Mussolini does not seem to be so reckless. Mussolini has repeatedly said that the scope of this meeting is limited to economics and does not involve politics. At the same time, there is also talk of expanding the meeting and recruiting the Little Entente. It can be seen that Mussolini's intention is only to target Germany and does not want to make the Little Entente feel uneasy. Moreover, Italy is the initiator of the Four-Power Pact and cannot abandon the treaty revision path stipulated by the Four-Power Pact and directly discuss the border issues of Central Europe with Austria and Hungary privately. Therefore, this meeting will not cause the hostility of the Little Entente. However, it is very difficult to win over the Little Entente to join the combination of Italy, Austria, and Hungary. If the Little Entente can cooperate with Austria and Hungary economically, then the economic problems of the Danube River basin can be solved to a considerable extent. It is not necessary for Italy to advocate for it today. Looking at the Treaty of Trianon, it clearly stipulates that Czechoslovakia can cooperate economically with Austria and Hungary for five years. However, due to the incompatibility, suspicion, and jealousy between the nations, this clause has become a dead letter. France also had a plan for Danube economic cooperation the year before last, but it failed because the Little Entente was unwilling to comply and Germany and Italy wanted to expand the scope. Based on this speculation, it can be known that the Little Entente will inevitably be difficult to join the combination of Italy, Austria, and Hungary in the future. In the future, the Little Entente will not be convenient to rely on Italy or to be close to Germany. Judging from the situation, in addition to seeking unity on its own, it may still have to collude with France.

In a word, whether the war in Europe breaks out or not depends on the policies of Germany, Italy, and Austria. If Germany can assess its strength and act cautiously, war can be avoided. If Italy has no intention of changing the border of Central Europe, war can also be avoided. If Austria does not restore the monarchy, war should have no reason to break out.

Yen Hui-ching Arrived in Beijing Yesterday

Will Go to Jiangxi to Visit Chiang Kai-shek Soon

(Nanjing) Yen Hui-ching, the ambassador to Russia, arrived in Pukou from Tianjin at 1 p.m. on the 15th and entered the city with his younger brother Deqing. He went to the official residence at No. 7 of the Ministry of Railways and rested briefly before taking a car to Beijige to visit Song Ziwen and talked for an hour. Then, he visited President Wang at the official residence and reported something. In the evening at 7 p.m., Minister Wang Guangqi and Chen Yanjiong, the director of the Pinghan Railway Bureau, held a banquet at Ming Yongchun to welcome Yen, and Vice Minister Xu Mo and the directors of various departments were invited to accompany him. Yen will go to Jiangxi soon to visit Chairman Chiang Kai-shek to report on the diplomatic situation between China and Russia and his personal opinions on diplomacy. He will also meet with Russian Ambassador Bogomolov in Beijing. The date of his return to Russia to resume his post has not yet been decided. According to the Russian Consulate, the Russian ambassador plans to meet Yen on the 16th in order to strengthen friendly relations. According to diplomatic circles, the meeting between Ambassador Yen and the Russian ambassador is only a social occasion in the international community and will at most only exchange opinions on ordinary diplomatic matters. (Special dispatch, 15th)

(Nanjing) Yen Hui-ching told reporters that he returned to China last month because he had family affairs to deal with, so he returned to Tianjin. Now that he has settled everything, he has specially come to Nanjing to visit the government authorities and discuss diplomatic issues in detail. He will stay in Beijing for a few days before going to Shanghai, Hangzhou, and other places to visit relatives and friends and go to Ji to visit Chiang Kai-shek to report on the international situation. However, the time has not yet been decided. He felt that the national concept of the people was very weak and that the national spirit was even more depressed, which was regrettable. At the beginning of the month, the traitor Puyi usurped the throne in Changchun, which did not attract the attention of the country, but the Japanese said that our ambition had become even more intensified. At that time, the Japanese army in Tianjin took the opportunity to hold exercises to demonstrate to us and extorted vehicles, making things difficult for us everywhere. Their intentions were even more sinister. At this time when the country's situation is precarious, the people of the whole country should be greatly enlightened, unite as one, and help the government to overcome the difficulties. They must not divide themselves and invite their own destruction. Yen also said that the difficulty of our country's situation today is known to everyone, but there is still room for diplomatic activity. However, there are many prescriptions, but I don't know if the patient is willing to take them. (Special dispatch, 15th)

(Xuzhou) Yen Hui-ching passed through Xuzhou on the Pingpu train this morning and went to Beijing. It is said that after Yen visits Wang, he will go to Shanghai. (Special dispatch, 15th)

Japanese Military Attaché Shibayama

Hosts a Banquet for the Beiping Press

(Beiping) Japanese Military Attaché Shibayama hosted a banquet for the Beiping press at Changchunting on the evening of the 15th, accompanied by Japanese Embassy Counselor Harada, Military Attaché Nemotoya, Ogi, and others. After taking their seats, Shibayama stood up and gave a speech, saying that the people of China and Japan were originally united as one, but due to less contact, they became estranged and could not understand each other. In the future, he hoped that they would support each other and promote the happiness of East Asia. Furthermore, Military Attaché Nemoto of our embassy will be transferred to the news section chief of the Ministry of the Army and will leave China. In the future, he will make contributions to the liaison and improvement of Chinese and Japanese news. If you have any instructions, he will accept them sincerely and welcome the Chinese press to visit our country for inspection. Today, I have prepared some drinks to wish you good health. There were also dancing and magic performances to add to the fun, and the banquet did not end until midnight. (Central News Agency dispatch, 15th)

Reception Held by He and Huang for Nakamura

Nakamura Returns to Tianjin from Beiping

(Beiping) He and Huang held a banquet tonight at the Foreign Ministry Building to bid farewell to Nakamura and invited important military and political figures to attend. (15th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Nakamura, the commander of the Japanese Garrison Army in North China, returned to Beiping yesterday from Gubeikou. This morning, he visited the Badaling section of the Great Wall via Nankou and Qinglongqiao, returning to Beiping in the afternoon. He will leave for Tianjin tomorrow morning to board a ship back to Japan and assume his new position as commander of the Sixth Division. Koiso, the Chief of Staff of the Kwantung Army, came to Beiping to visit our military and political authorities and is also scheduled to return to Changchun tomorrow morning before returning to Japan to take up his new position as commander of the Fifth Division. (15th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Nakamura Kotaro went from Tianjin to Beiping some days ago and then went to Gubeikou to inspect the Japanese garrison. He returned to Tianjin from Beiping at 7 p.m. on the 15th. It is reported that his successor, Meimura Meijiro, has already departed from Tokyo and is expected to arrive in Tianjin around the 19th to take office. Nakamura will return to Japan after completing the handover. (15th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Beiping) Nakamura took the Ping-Sui special train to Nankou and Qinglongqiao on the morning of the 15th to visit Badaling. He returned to Beiping in the afternoon and returned to Tianjin at 4 o'clock. (15th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Tianjin) The newly appointed Japanese commander of the Tianjin Garrison, Meijiro Umezu, departed from Tokyo on the 14th to take up his post. Nakamura returned to Tianjin from Beiping this morning to await the handover. (15th Special Dispatch)

Tang Youren

Secret Talks with Huang Fu Yesterday

(Beiping) Tang Youren visited Huang Fu this morning for a lengthy secret talk. Huang is holding a banquet at the Yingbin Hotel tonight. (15th Special Dispatch)

Ariyoshi's Return to Japan Still Uncertain

(Nanjing) There has been no notification of Ariyoshi's return to Japan. According to established practice, when an ambassador returns to his country, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs must be notified of who will act as chargé d'affaires. Therefore, the official date of Ariyoshi's return to Japan cannot be confirmed. (15th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Executive Yuan Orders Expedition

Establishment of the Mongolian Political Affairs Committee

Four Guiding Principles Indicated

Mongolian Representatives Call on He and Huang in Beiping

(Nanjing) The Executive Yuan ordered the early establishment of the Mongolian Local Autonomy Political Affairs Committee and indicated four guiding principles: (1) After the establishment of the committee, it should quickly draft plans for implementing various construction projects and prepare a budget; (2) Mongolian personnel should be appointed as much as possible, but those who have benefited the local area in the past or are respected by the Mongolians should be selected; (3) Finances must be open and thrifty; (4) Education must be actively promoted. (15th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Enkhbat submitted a request to the Executive Yuan to resign from the Mongolian Autonomous Political Affairs Committee. (15th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Zhao Daiwen, the deputy director of Mongolian Local Autonomy Guidance, sent a telegram to Lin Wang on the 13th stating that he was incompetent and undeserving of the honor and deeply feared that he would not be able to fulfill his duties. He would do his best and consult with Director He on everything and follow his instructions. He sent this telegram to express his gratitude. On the 14th, Wang replied to Zhao, saying that after the implementation of Mongolian Local Autonomy, he relied on the guidance of experienced people to achieve soundness. He was deeply grateful for Mr. Zhao's enthusiasm in taking on this important responsibility and was particularly pleased. (15th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Nima Otesor and fifteen other representatives of various Mongolian leagues and banners who had come to the capital returned to Beiping the day before yesterday. This afternoon, they separately called on He and Huang to urge He to quickly take office as the director of Inner Mongolian Autonomy Guidance. Nima and others decided to leave Beiping on the 21st to return to Bailingmiao and jointly notify the representatives, princes, and youths of various leagues and banners who attended the Mongolian Autonomy Conference in Bailingmiao to gather in Bailingmiao on a fixed date for a meeting. Nima and others will report in detail on the results of the representatives' visit to Wang and Chiang in Nanjing and the satisfactory results of Inner Mongolian Autonomy. The date of the meeting will be decided after Nima and others return to Bailingmiao, probably no later than mid-April. At that time, if He is unable to personally attend and guide the meeting, he may send a representative who is familiar with Mongolian affairs to guide everything. (15th Special Dispatch)

(Taiyuan) Zhao Daiwen has telegraphed the central government, agreeing to take the post of deputy director of Inner Mongolia Guidance and telegraphed He to discuss the date of taking office. Mongolian representatives and others have sent telegrams of congratulations. However, according to Zhao, he is old and weak and will not be able to go to Beiping for the time being. Xinjiang Construction Association

Holds Second Meeting

President Wang Attends and Addresses the Meeting

(Nanjing) The Xinjiang Construction Planning Committee held its second meeting at 2 p.m. on the 15th, with 47 people present. Chu Minyi chaired the meeting, and President Wang also attended and addressed the meeting, saying that the government considers the Xinjiang issue to be extremely important and has established the Construction Committee to gather people familiar with the situation in Xinjiang to jointly study the construction of Xinjiang. The most important thing is to develop transportation and build railways, which is a fundamental solution, but it requires funds and time. The initial solution is to build roads for automobiles. Secondly, Xinjiang's finances are extremely chaotic and need to be reorganized urgently. The nationalities are complex, and their development and ability should be supported. All of these issues are expected to be studied in detail and contributed as much as possible. As for the military and political affairs of Xinjiang, the central government is planning effective solutions and will not use force as the only tool. However, the diplomatic power should be centralized. The central government has taken over the various consulates established by the provincial government in the Soviet Union, etc. Then, the outline of the construction plan and the work procedures were discussed, and it was decided to divide them into four groups, and the members were asked to identify the groups. The chairman appointed the conveners, including Tang Kesan and Zhang Ximan for the political group, Chen Zengliang and Luo Jing for the economic group, Wang Zengshan and Liu Lunying for the cultural group, and Li Jingcong and Feng Youzhen for the transportation group. The detailed items of the outline will be discussed at the third meeting on the 17th. The work procedures are roughly divided into three stages: organization, preparation, and completion, which are scheduled to be completed in three months. (15th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Three-Headed Meeting at Villa d'Este

Guaranteeing the Independence of Austria and Hungary

Full Discussion of Mussolini's Policies

Economic Transformation of the Danube River

Italy Has Lofty Ambitions

German Foreign Minister Quietly Goes to Rome with an Important Mission

Rome The three-headed meeting of the prime ministers of Italy, Austria, and Hungary made significant progress on Thursday afternoon. This morning, the King of Italy entertained the two distinguished guests with a grand banquet at the Royal Palace. In the afternoon, the three prime ministers held their first meeting at Villa d'Este, where they had a full discussion of "Mussolini's policies." The purpose is to maintain the economic and political independence of Austria and Hungary and to create an Italian sphere of influence in the upper reaches of the Danube River. (15th National Telegram)

(Berlin) German Foreign Minister Neurath quietly left Berlin for Rome yesterday. It is reported that he will meet with Italian Prime Minister Mussolini to discuss the Nazi Party's incident in Austria. The purpose of this trip is to discuss the current situation between Germany and Austria with the Italian Prime Minister and Austrian Chancellor Dollfuss and Hungarian Prime Minister Gömbös. It is reported that the German Foreign Minister's trip also carries an important mission from German Chancellor Hitler. He will discuss with Italy the possibility of Germany rejoining the League of Nations within two years of its withdrawal from the League of Nations, if necessary. (15th National Telegram)

Rome The Prime Ministers of Italy, Hungary, and Austria continued to meet in Rome today to discuss assisting Hungary and Austria in suppressing Germany's cunning plan to annex the two countries through the Nazi Party. It is said that German Vice-Chancellor Papen will also attend the meeting on Thursday to explain Germany's position and consolidate Germany's position. According to news from here today, Prime Minister Mussolini proposed that Trieste and Fiume be designated as free zones for Germany, Austria, and Hungary. Mussolini's move has two purposes: first, to undermine Germany's control over exports from Hungary and Austria; second, to restore the priority of railway transportation between Trieste and Fiume to Austria, so as to compete with the railway from Vienna to Hamburg, Germany. The railway from Vienna to Hamburg is an important route for Hungary and Austria to reach northern ports. (15th National Telegram)

Rome Prime Minister Mussolini met with Hungarian Prime Minister Gömbös yesterday and Austrian Chancellor Dollfuss today, but the three have not yet met at the same time. According to general opinion, the outcome of the talks between the three countries will be nothing more than the publication of a joint declaration, reaffirming the friendly relations between the three countries, and not the conclusion of an agreement of a political nature. As for economic matters, the three prime ministers are unlikely to conclude an agreement of a definitive nature, such as a commercial treaty. What is planned is a non-triangular organization, which other countries such as Czechoslovakia and Germany can join after its establishment. The three countries are also striving to reach an understanding on the issue of the economic reorganization of the Danube River countries. This work is based on the Italian memorandum of September 29 last year. The Italian government sent notes to the signatory countries of the Four-Power Pact and the countries that became independent after the dissolution of the old Austro-Hungarian Empire (i.e., Austria, Hungary, Czechoslovakia, and Yugoslavia), suggesting that the economic reorganization of the Danube River countries be carried out and expanded in accordance with the method decided by the Stresa Conference the year before, and that it be applied uniformly to most agricultural products. (14th Havas News Agency Telegram)

Rome This morning, Austrian Chancellor Dollfuss laid a wreath at the Italian Royal Mausoleum and the Tomb of the Unknown Soldier. At noon, he had a secret talk with Italian Prime Minister Mussolini, and then attended the banquet of Sir Mada. According to semi-official news, Italy's "Danube River Policy" towards Italy, Austria, and Hungary is the same as the policy of the Little Entente countries, and seeks mutual understanding so that they can respond to each other. The meeting between Italian Prime Minister Mussolini and the two Prime Ministers Dollfuss and Gömbös is scheduled to be held tomorrow afternoon. Tomorrow at noon, they will attend the Italian King's luncheon. This afternoon, the three cabinet ministers and the King of Siam visited the cavalry school to watch equestrian performances. At 6 p.m., Prime Ministers Gömbös and Dollfuss will meet and have a long secret talk in the Grand Hotel. In the evening, Dollfuss and the Italian ambassador to Austria will be received by the Roman Pope, and then attend Mussolini's grand banquet. In addition to the two state guests, all senior officials and all diplomatic envoys were invited to the banquet. Tomorrow night, the two distinguished guests will be invited to watch a play at the Royal Theatre of Bayreuth. (14th National Telegram)

Morning Before Yesterday

Held Preparatory Meeting

Agreed on the Basis for Economic Negotiations

Revision of Treaty Not Expected to Be Discussed

London No important news came out of Rome yesterday. The Prime Ministers of Italy, Austria, and Hungary are scheduled to hold their first official meeting this afternoon to discuss how to guarantee the continued independence of Austria and Hungary economically and politically. A preparatory meeting was held yesterday, the most important of which was the meeting between the Italian Prime Minister and the Austrian Chancellor in the morning, where they reportedly discussed the method of tariff preferences and quotas between Italy and Austria, and the convenience that Austria and Hungary could enjoy in Trieste and Fiume. It is reported that Italy is willing to buy more Austrian machinery and industrial products, while Austria is willing to buy more Italian agricultural products, especially wine, but not much grain, because Austria will buy grain from Hungary. The Hungarian Prime Minister also had a long talk with the Austrian Chancellor yesterday morning, and then went to see the German Ambassador to Italy.

Last night, the Austrian Chancellor told reporters that the joint plan is now under discussion and should be announced before Easter. It is reported that the revision of the treaty was not discussed yesterday, and may not be discussed even at today's meeting.

Afternoon Visit to Cavalry Drills

This afternoon, the three prime ministers, along with the King of Siam and others, watched the horsemanship performance at the Cavalry School. In the evening, the Roman Pope summoned the Austrian Chancellor to inquire about the recent situation in Austria. (15th Reuters Telegram)

It is Reported That Italian Military Supplies

Go From Austria to Hungary

Causing Panic Among the Danube Countries

Austrian Home Guard Concentrated and Waiting for Orders

(London) The Danube countries are greatly alarmed by the rumor that Italian military supplies are being transported to Hungary. Although the official arena in Vienna has tried hard to refute this rumor, it persists. It is said that two trains fully loaded with military supplies passed through Austria and entered Hungary on March 8 and 9. A newspaper in the capital of Yugoslavia even claimed that there was evidence that military supplies were indeed transported from Italy to Austria. If Italy takes such action, it will be impossible for the Little Entente countries to participate in economic cooperation. It is now planned to ask the League of Nations to control the military equipment of Austria and Hungary. Officials in the Hungarian capital pointed out that this rumor has no basis. Hungarian newspapers said that this rumor originated in the Little Entente countries with the aim of disrupting the current negotiations in Rome. Austrian Chancellor Dollfuss is currently in Rome, and the leader of the Austrian Home Guard reorganized his subordinates in Vienna yesterday, reportedly intending to concentrate all his forces under Vice-Chancellor Fey. (15th Reuters Telegram)

Austrian Restoration Movement

Methods of Struggle Do Not Go Beyond the Scope of the Law

Only Seek the Restoration of the Royal Family and Oppose the Union of Austria and Hungary

Vienna Weissner, one of the leaders of the Austrian monarchist legitimists, explained the current situation of the Habsburg royal family's restoration to representatives of Austrian and foreign newspapers here. Weissner solemnly stated that once the Austrian order banning the entry of the old royal family is lifted, the royal family will immediately return to reside in their own country. He also said that the methods of struggle used by the legitimists will never go beyond the scope of the law. He rejected the claim that Austria and Hungary should implement a monarchical union system, because the legitimists only seek the Austrian throne. (14th Havas News Agency Telegram)

Whether the British Plan is Accepted

The Success or Failure of the Disarmament Issue Depends On This

Eden Spoke Eloquently in the House of Commons

Hope that Britain, the United States, and Japan Maintain Close Cooperation

The British Conservative Party Advocates Swift Action to Negotiate an Air Force Agreement

A Convention, Even If Incomplete, is Better Than Nothing

The French Foreign Affairs Committee Passed a Resolution Opposing German Military Build-Up

Insisting on Implementing Disarmament Under a Monitoring System

France's Reply to Britain's Note Postponed Until the End of Next Week

(London) Sir Eden stated in the House of Commons today that since his visits to the authorities of various European countries, he has become more convinced that the success or failure of the Disarmament Conference depends on whether or not the countries can accept the British plan. The British plan has been detailed in the recent disarmament memorandum submitted to the countries. Eden's response to the Labour Party's attacks on the government's remarks was very painful. The Labour Party believes that the government lacks decisiveness and understanding of the Disarmament Conference, which has aroused external fears of war. Eden continued, saying that the government will study the replies from Italy, France, and Germany with a sympathetic and understanding attitude. The government also firmly believes that the countries of the world will not want the failure of the Disarmament Conference. Eden also said that what he heard in Paris, Berlin, and Rome makes him more convinced that the successful agreement of the Disarmament Conference is none other than the British Disarmament Memorandum. Qiang accused Foreign Minister Simon of expressing a lukewarm attitude towards the US disarmament proposal. Simon denied this, saying that the US has never made any consideration of being on an equal footing with Germany in disarmament matters. Outsiders claim that the US is unwilling to cooperate with the countries in seeking the success of the Disarmament Conference. Eden pointed out that this statement is absurd. Eden declared that the US has been of great help in drafting the treaty in the disarmament discussions. One point that the Disarmament Conference is encouraging is the close cooperation between Britain and the United States. Observers believe that Britain, the United States, and Japan will prepare for the largest naval competition in history. In terms of shipbuilding plans, the United States is of course the only one. However, the US warships are already outdated, so it is doubtful whether the US can occupy a leading position. (15th National Telegram)

(London) The Lord Privy Seal of England, Eden, today described his European tour to promote disarmament in the House of Commons, and his words were quite optimistic, saying that it is not easy to reconcile the opinions of France and Germany, but it is not yet possible to be pessimistic when the documents in response to the British proposal have not been fully received. When a member asked if there was no hope of trying to reconcile the opinions of France and Germany, Eden replied in the negative and was not disappointed. Eden also said that misrepresentation is a mistake. If the Disarmament Conference fails, not only will the security of the European countries be shaken, but the security of the United Kingdom will also be in danger. After the failure of the Disarmament Conference, the countries will inevitably be eager to reorganize their armaments, and the United Kingdom is even more so, because the United Kingdom has automatically disarmed a lot. He believed that even if the United Kingdom increased its armaments several times, it might not be able to guarantee the security of the United Kingdom alone. Why? Because the competition between armaments will ultimately be insecure. What is urgently needed is a convention based on the British proposal and the restoration of the full authority of the League of Nations, with all the major countries of Western Europe listed in it. The British government will give sympathetic consideration to the documents of the countries that respond to the British proposal, and have the confidence that the countries do not want the Disarmament Conference to break down. When Eden mentioned the Prussian Prime Minister Goering's statement that "the Prussian spirit will eventually dominate Germany's future," he frankly prepared to recognize the difference between a military country and a militaristic country. But he felt that from the perspective of the British people, Goering's words belonged more to the militaristic country than to the military country. (Applause from the audience)

After Eden finished speaking, the members of the House of Commons began to debate foreign affairs. Churchill spoke first, saying that if the government thought that Prime Minister MacDonald's plan could be accepted by the people, it would be deceiving itself. The great danger of today's foreign policy is that we demand that France weaken its armaments, and the organization of international troops under the League of Nations is impossible. However, the troops of various countries may be able to contact each other for special reasons and give the world security. Labour Party member Wilson said that Eden's intention was excellent, but in view of the ambitions of German adventurers, he felt that Eden's efforts were a little untimely. Liberal Party member Samuel said that the revival of German militarism has placed Europe in a terrible dilemma. Will Europe tacitly approve its development until a world catastrophe occurs, or will it not recognize its equal status and stop its development? (14th Reuters Telegram)

Foreign Minister Simon ended the debate, vaguely saying, "If the general convention on disarmament cannot be successful, then we should try to negotiate an air force agreement with the countries of Western Europe. However, the United Kingdom is forced to be in this situation, and we will never allow the negotiations to drag on for a long time and have no end. What is important now is to act quickly. If a better solution is finally hopeless, then we can only calculate for the United Kingdom based on the results that the situation can produce in order to quickly deal with the needs of the situation." Simon believes that the method of secretly reorganizing armaments is very harmful, so he also said that in his opinion, "a disarmament convention, even if incomplete, is a hundred times better than no convention at all." (14th Havas News Agency Telegram)

(Paris) After exchanging views on the diplomatic situation, the Foreign Affairs Committee of the House of Representatives submitted a resolution, which was passed by the whole body, with only one abstention. The content of this resolution is as follows: (1) It still supports the implementation of disarmament under international supervision, as in the past policy, but it must be carried out under organized security conditions; (2) It continues to oppose Germany's military build-up; (3) It extremely hopes to conclude a general disarmament convention. If a convention cannot be concluded, then a convention should be concluded with the goal of limiting armaments, so as to avoid countries competing in armaments again and endangering peace. (14th Havas News Agency Telegram)

(Paris) According to news from responsible parties, France's reply to the British disarmament statement may be sent out at the end of next week. The wording of this reply is mainly to avoid closing the door to future solutions. It is reported that the general conditions contained in the letter of former Foreign Minister Barthou to the Chairman of the Disarmament Conference Henderson on February 10 will be recognized. France is eager to prevent the disarmament discussions from miscarrying and deeply hopes that this reply can facilitate the final agreement. However, France's minimum needs, namely security and effective management of armaments, still need to be understood by the United Kingdom. All future matters depend on this. (14th Reuters Telegram)

Taking Advantage of the Opportunity of Disarmament Failure

Russia Launches a Peace Offensive

Will Propose a Universal Non-Aggression Pact

Promote Diplomatic Relations with France and Leave Japan in Isolation

(London) Regarding the contents of the Soviet Union's "peace offensive" plan after the failure of the disarmament negotiations disclosed in today's Daily Telegraph, the Daily Telegraph has always been known for its well-informed diplomatic news. According to the newspaper, the Soviet Union advocates the conclusion of a universal non-aggression pact, with a mutual assistance pact to sanction aggressors attached. As for the definition of aggression, it is still based on the Eight-Nation Pact signed in London last summer. The Soviet Union hopes that this will further isolate Japan, because Japan is unwilling to participate in such a pact. The Soviet Union also hopes to use this to promote diplomatic relations with France, because France can be expected to welcome the Soviet Union's proposal. As for the United Kingdom, it is unlikely to participate in this pact because of the provisions of restraint, so as not to increase its responsibilities. (14th National Telegram)

Roosevelt's Plan

Reorganization of Aviation Agencies

Eliminating Redundancy and Increasing Combat Effectiveness

Now is the Time to Reform the Air Force

Lin and White Decline Investigation Committee Positions

(Washington) According to reliable sources in official circles, President Roosevelt is currently planning a practical merger of government aviation agencies. The White House has confirmed this, stating that a new plan for aviation organization is currently being drafted. President Roosevelt believes that the U.S. Air Force agencies are too redundant, which is uneconomical and inefficient. Merging these redundant agencies into one would benefit the Army, Navy, and private aviation. It is said that General Mitchell may be the commander of this new organization. Mitchell has long been a proponent of merging the Army, Navy, and Air Force. The reason he left the military was due to his severe criticism of the Air Force's division. Senator Max Howe stated that without unified action, the United States would be unable to fight. Howe also cited the deaths encountered by the U.S. Air Force mail service to illustrate the current state of the U.S. Air Force. Howe's remarks are approximately as follows: "We all know that the outcome of future wars will be determined by the superiority of the Air Force. We also know that the United States must quickly prepare for aerial warfare. The unpreparedness of the United States is enough to invite foreign attacks. All countries in the world must know that the United States is prepared. Now is the time. I believe that both the Senate and the House of Representatives are ready for correct military legislation." Secretary of the Navy Swanson expressed opposition to the merger of the Navy Air Force with other air forces, believing that the nature of the Army Air Force and the Navy Air Force is completely different. The restoration of Air Force mail service is still pending, as the Chief of the Air Corps of the War Department, General Foulois, is currently conducting an investigation of airmail lines in the eastern half of the United States. Foulois will also inspect the equipment of the troops. Foulois declared that the order to restore airmail would not be issued until after his inspection is complete. Today, the Senate Post Office Committee invited Lindbergh, Chamberlain, Rickenbacker, and Brigadier General Mikel to a meeting to consult on various legislative opinions regarding returning airmail to private operation. (14th National Telegram)

(New York) The famous American aviator Lindbergh was recently appointed by the Secretary of War as a member of the Aviation Investigation Committee, but according to today's news, Lindbergh declined to serve, stating that in his view, it is inappropriate to use Army planes to transport mail, and it is unfair to commercially run airmail companies because the commercial contracts were revoked without proper review. (15th Reuters Telegram)

Minister of the Army, Lin

Explains Sino-Russian Situation

Says Situation Has Not Reached Critical Point

(Tokyo) In today's House of Representatives session, Ryuuji Nagashima of the Seiyukai Party first raised questions about the proposal to reduce the Manchurian Incident reserve fund in this year's budget, and then questioned the relationship between Manchuria and Russia. Minister of the Army Lin responded as follows:

Judging solely from the current situation of the Manchurian-Russian border relationship, it seems that the Soviet Union has a tendency towards proactive actions, but this cannot be said to mean that the Soviet Union is preparing for an offensive, as there is no factual evidence to prove this.

Soviet personnel operating on the front lines of the Manchurian-Soviet border have either shot down Japanese planes or frequently appeared in Korean territory. Their transgressions should indeed be recognized as facts. However, the political and diplomatic relations between Japan and the Soviet Union have not yet reached a critical situation, so there is no cause for concern.

As for the Manchurian Incident expenses, they are funds used to maintain peace and order in Manchuria. If 10 million yen is not enough, additional budget will still be requested. (15th Rengo Telegram)

Japan Actively Pursuing

Economic Aggression Policy

Dividing the World into Four Zones

(Tokyo) It is reported that the government is currently considering the following plan to actively promote trade and intelligence agencies:

(1) Divide the world into four zones and establish economic officials at the director-general level in London, New York, Mumbai, and Shanghai, key locations. Under them will be specialists from the Ministry of Finance, Ministry of Commerce and Industry, Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry, etc., who will liaise with correspondents in key locations to investigate the economies of various countries.

(2) Establish an Economic Research Bureau directly under the Cabinet to centralize the above-mentioned reports, and at the same time investigate domestic industries, study the comparison of new and old goods, and the potential for future conflicts. In case of an emergency, preparations should be made immediately and concrete measures should be sought.

(3) Investigate overseas affairs and encourage and guide trade.

(4) Regarding diplomatic negotiations on disputes, the economic officials and related officials in charge of the region will serve as plenipotentiary economic advisors and begin activities. (15th Den-tsu Telegram)

After Breakdown of Cotton Industry Negotiations

Britain and Japan Both Advocate Caution

(Paris) According to the Economic and Financial News Agency, the Lancashire cotton industry delegation met yesterday with Sir Wilson, representative of Trade Minister Runciman. The delegation is now preparing to submit a report to the government. The report will recommend several measures to be taken, but it is generally believed that these measures will not be too hasty. The British government does not advocate applying differential treatment to tariffs on Japanese goods or stipulating restrictions on the amount of Japanese goods imported. Increasing export taxes on Japanese goods would inevitably raise local prices in some British colonies, and the British government's aim is to revive the export trade of Lancashire cotton cloth. Adopting tariff policies would run counter to this aim. Japan, on the other hand, is also maintaining caution and does not want to fall into political and economic isolation. Therefore, it is expected that direct negotiations between Britain and Japan are still possible. It is reported that Trade Minister Runciman will soon meet with the Japanese Ambassador to the United Kingdom to discuss the matter. (15th Havas Telegram)

(London) The breakdown of the Anglo-Japanese textile negotiations will be a matter for diplomatic discussion between the British and Japanese governments. Secretary of the Board of Trade Hore-Belisha stated in the House of Commons today that he would visit Japanese Ambassador Matsudaira to handle the matter. Before the start of the negotiations, Hore-Belisha stayed in Manchester for two days to discuss the competition of Japanese cotton goods. Also, Hore-Belisha stated that the British representatives had submitted their report to the government yesterday afternoon. Since the negotiations were the result of discussions between the British and Japanese governments and have now failed, the government will still consider the matter, but it is not convenient to say more at this time. (15th Reuters Telegram)

Japanese Budget Approved

Movement to Overthrow Cabinet Intensifies Again

Saito Decides to Visit Elder Statesman Saionji

(Tokyo) The budget for this emergency situation reached a huge sum of 2.112 billion yen and was declared established on the 14th. Therefore, the government is working hard to pass important bills so that both houses may not need to extend the session and can conclude it. It is especially important to focus all efforts on the House of Peers in order to promote this. However, as the deadline for the closing of the Diet is approaching, the behind-the-scenes machinations in the political world are gradually intensifying. It is difficult to be optimistic about the atmosphere inside the Diet and the movement to overthrow the cabinet outside the Diet. Therefore, the government has decided that after the closing of the Diet, Prime Minister Saito will visit Duke Saionji to state the handling of the future political situation and attempt to reorganize the cabinet in order to stabilize the political situation. However, judging from the objective situation, the lifespan of the Saito cabinet is quite questionable. (15th Japanese Union Telegram)

Sixty-Six Dead

Sasebo As of 11 p.m. on the 14th, the torpedo boat Tomozuru had a total of 13 survivors rescued, 4 officers and 62 non-commissioned officers and sailors recovered dead, 2 unrecovered dead, and 32 missing, including Commander Iwase. (15th Japanese Union Telegram)

U.S.-Central American Five-Nation Conference

Discussing Broad Plan for Economic Alliance

U.S. Sends Special Representative to Attend as Observer

Guatemala City Representatives of the five republics of Central America—Guatemala, El Salvador, Honduras, Nicaragua, and Costa Rica—will meet tomorrow to discuss the broad plan for an economic alliance proposed by the government of Guatemala. The main points are: (1) a simple monetary standard, (2) unified tariffs, (3) abolition of passports, (4) facilitation of naturalization, (5) removal of various obstacles to occupational exercise, and (6) simple diplomatic duties. The United States has been invited to send a representative to attend the meeting as an observer or advisor. (14th Reuters Telegram)

El Salvador

Explosives Stored in Cellar Explode

Over One Hundred Dead, Countless Injured

Island of El Salvador, Central America Today, 250 boxes of explosives stored in a cellar suddenly exploded, killing over one hundred people and injuring countless others. Most of the buildings were destroyed by the explosion. (15th Reuters Telegram)

Morocco

Oil Well Fire Not Extinguished

Oil Flows Down Mountain Like a Fiery Serpent

Engineers Try to Put Out Fire Without Success

Tangier Two years ago, French engineers drilled wells in the Zirfa Mountains near Tangier, French Morocco, to extract oil. Last week, oil gushed out, yielding about 600,000 gallons per hour. Unexpectedly, the oil that spewed out touched an electric wire, the wire broke, and a fire started. Thus, where the oil reached, the fire followed, resulting in a river of fire flowing down the mountain, covering a wide area. The villages at the foot of the mountain are in danger. Engineers are now planning to blast a section of the mountain in order to block the oil well.

Also, the fire in the Zirfa Mountains has not subsided. Although engineers used half a ton of gunpowder to bomb the hillside above the oil well in an attempt to block the well, it was ultimately ineffective. (14th Reuters Telegram)

Situation Turns from Danger to Safety

Strike Wave Gradually Subsides

Madrid The printing strike has ended. Evening newspapers will be published tomorrow, and morning newspapers will be published on Friday morning. However, the newspaper ABC is still being boycotted, but the newspaper can still be published. The construction industry in the Galicia region, which declared a strike in response to the workers in Madrid, has now ended. (15th Havas Telegram)

U.S. Warship Mishap Details

British Warship's Effective Assistance

Distressed Officers and Soldiers Transported to Port

(Hong Kong) The U.S. Far East flagship USS Luzon was burned 30 miles southwest of Hong Kong on the morning of the 14th due to an oil line explosion. Hong Kong dispatched a warship to rescue it. It was towed back to Hong Kong for repairs on the afternoon of the 15th. Eight injured soldiers were sent to the hospital. The hull was severely damaged. (15th Special Telegram)

(Hong Kong) When the U.S. warship USS Rutherton approached Dapeng Bay on the afternoon of the 14th, the engine room suddenly exploded, and the entire ship caught fire. The officers and soldiers fled to boats. The Hong Kong Navy, upon hearing the news, dispatched the HMS Wishart to provide assistance. All 187 officers and soldiers safely arrived in Hong Kong. Eight were seriously injured and hospitalized. The ship was towed back to Hong Kong for repairs on the morning of the 15th. (15th Central News Agency Telegram)

(Hong Kong) The officers and sailors of the U.S. gunboat USS Rutherton have left the ship to go to the lifeboats today. The gunboat has been destroyed. The ship was originally tasked with suppressing pirates, but unexpectedly a fire broke out on board. Efforts to extinguish the fire were ineffective, and the fire spread to the powder magazine. The captain ordered everyone to leave the ship and board the lifeboats and sent out a distress signal. Soon, many ships arrived one after another. The British destroyers HMS Wishart, HMS White Fly, and the ship Tainan arrived first and rescued everyone in the lifeboats. Two lifeboats were lost due to fog, but fortunately they were found soon and arrived safely in Hong Kong. There were 15 officers, 125 sailors, and 30 marines. The cause of the fire was reportedly from the oil depot. In an instant, the flames lit up the sky and could be seen from several miles away. The hull was completely destroyed and soon sank. After arriving in Hong Kong, the officers of the U.S. warship praised the bravery of the officers of the British warship who rescued them at the scene. Currently, eight sailors from the Rutherton are in the hospital for treatment, but their injuries are not serious. (15th National News Agency Telegram)

(Hong Kong) Yesterday, the U.S. warship USS Rutherton (1,100 tons) had an accident in Dapeng Bay. After everyone on the ship boarded the lifeboats at 10 a.m., they were rescued by the British destroyers HMS Wishart and Jinan (transliteration). At the time of the accident, there was a heavy fog, but fortunately everyone on the ship was rescued. Only three people were injured: one was burned by steam, one broke an arm, and one broke a leg. HMS Wishart arrived in Hong Kong at 2:40 a.m. this morning, carrying U.S. warship Captain McHenry and all the crew members. Today, a Reuters reporter interviewed Captain Fillon of the U.S. warship and heard about the accident. According to him, the fire started in the engine room at 6:35 p.m. yesterday. Everyone on the ship was having dinner at the time. So an alarm was sounded once. Later, the fire became fierce, so an alarm was sounded again, ordering all personnel to board the deck. A quarter of an hour later, the rear of the ship was separated from the front, and the radio was also damaged at that time. At that time, the ship Jinan arrived first and fired rockets to guide HMS Wishart. Captain Fillon praised the bravery of Captain Duterte of the British warship and said that because the British captain risked docking HMS Wishart near the U.S. warship, everyone was able to escape one by one. As for the personnel at the stern of the ship, they all jumped onto the wooden rafts released by the British warship. At the same time, the ship Jinan also rescued two small boats carrying sailors. After arriving in Hong Kong, the personnel of the U.S. warship mustered on the British warship HMS Campbelltown and then went ashore in formation. The officers were stationed on HMS Campbelltown and HMS Daoma. HMS Wishart is currently docked next to the U.S. warship, fearing that the fire cannot be extinguished within 24 hours. The ship's powder magazine was flooded at the time of the accident, so there is no risk of explosion. (15th Reuters Telegram)

(Hong Kong) The naval tugboat USS Chaser is now sailing to Dapeng Bay, preparing to tow the U.S. gunboat USS Rutherton back near Hong Kong. The U.S. Consul General in Hong Kong published an article in the press today, expressing his gratitude to the Navy and the British warship HMS Wishart and all parties for assisting the U.S. gunboat USS Rutherton. Due to the inclement weather, another tugboat is rushing to Dapeng Bay to assist the USS Chaser in towing the U.S. warship back. It is estimated that the U.S. warship can be towed to Hong Kong this afternoon. (15th Reuters Telegram)

Legislative Yuan Reviews

Railway Construction Bonds

(Nanjing) The Finance Committee of the Legislative Yuan held a meeting on the 15th to review the Railway Construction Bonds Bill. Chairman Ma Yinchu stated that the Ministry of Railways' request to issue railway construction bonds only stated that they were for managing old roads and building new roads. As a result of the discussion, Chen Changheng, Wei Tingsheng, Shi Weishen and others were assigned to conduct a preliminary review, and the Ministry of Railways was requested to send personnel to attend the meeting to explain their opinions. (15th Special Telegram)

Local Laws and Regulations of Provinces and Cities

Uniform Implementation Measures

(Nanjing) The Executive Yuan has approved the uniform implementation measures for single-item regulations in various provinces. The measures are as follows: (1) Any single-item regulations formulated by provincial and municipal governments that restrict the freedom of the people or increase their burden, even if approved by the provincial and municipal councils, must still be submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval before being promulgated and implemented. Any regulations not submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval will have no effect. (2) The single-item regulations submitted for approval as described in the preceding paragraph will be reviewed by the relevant ministries and commissions of the Executive Yuan according to their nature, and a report will be submitted to the Executive Yuan for review and instructions. (3) If provincial and municipal governments have any opinions on the regulations approved by the Executive Yuan, they may still submit their opinions and request revisions, which will be promulgated and implemented after approval. (4) The date of promulgation of all approved regulations must be submitted to the Executive Yuan and the relevant ministries and commissions for record at the same time. (5) Single-item regulations that do not concern the freedom and burden of the people will be formulated and promulgated directly by the provincial and municipal governments, and will be submitted to the Executive Yuan and the relevant ministries and commissions for record at the same time. (Special dispatch from the 15th)

Passed by the Examination Yuan

Qualified Candidates

(Nanjing) The Examination Yuan held a meeting on the morning of the 15th, chaired by Wang Yongbin, and resolved the following important cases: (1) Approved 12 persons qualified for the higher examination; (2) Approved 55 persons qualified for the general examination; (3) Regarding the application of the applicant Lu Honghuang, requesting an interpretation of whether the graduation qualifications of Shanghai Qunzhi University can be used to take the general examination, it was resolved to send a letter to the Ministry of Judicial Administration to inquire whether the qualifications of graduates from the school are recognized, and then decide. In addition, the metropolitan general examination, originally scheduled to end on March 20th, has been extended to the end of March due to numerous requests from outside the capital. Control Yuan

Impeachment of Yellow River Affairs Personnel

(Nanjing) Control Committee member Yang Rentian impeached Zhou Xiangxian, a member of the Yellow River Disaster Relief Committee, and Sun Qingze, director of the Yellow River Affairs Bureau of Hebei, for neglecting their duties and harming the people. After review, it was generally believed that the government had allocated a large amount of money, appointed committee members, and established a special bureau, originally to be responsible for Yellow River disaster relief. The committee members and bureau director should have been prudent and careful in carrying out flood prevention and rescue work to mitigate disasters. However, in Changyuan County, Hebei, the breach at Shitouzhuan was not blocked, resulting in another tragic disaster. This was an extreme case of negligence and should be immediately transferred to the disciplinary committee to emphasize the importance of people's lives. The Control Yuan has transferred the case to the Central Public Disciplinary Committee for investigation and handling. (Special dispatch from the 15th)

(Nanjing) The Control Yuan sent a telegram to the governments of Hebei, Shandong, and Henan provinces stating that, according to a telegram from Shao Hongji and Yu Hongqi, the lack of ships to transport materials and the resulting delays along the way were the biggest reasons for the delay in the construction of the Changyuan blockade project. During the spring floods, the water势 [shì - power/momentum] was raging, and the work of closing the gap was urgent. If relief measures were not taken quickly, the effects might be delayed, and the disaster situation might inevitably worsen. It was proposed to quickly telegraph the governments of Hebei, Shandong, and Henan provinces to instruct the relevant county bureaus along the Yellow River from Gongxian to Zhengxian to find ways to recruit and send heavy-load ships to the Second Engineering Office for application, so as to avoid delaying important work, etc. Please investigate and comply as soon as possible. (Special dispatch from the 15th)

Annual Interest of Five Percent to Be Paid Off in Five Years

(Jinan) Shanghai and Shandong silk merchants held another meeting at the Construction Department today and resolved to issue 400,000 yuan of public bonds to subsidize Chen silk, with an annual interest rate of 5%, to be paid off in five years starting next year. The bonds will be issued after approval from the provincial government. (Special dispatch from the 15th)

Wuhan City Plans to Establish a National Goods Shopping Mall

(Hankou) The Wuhan city government plans to establish a national goods shopping mall and has decided to allocate public land and 50,000 yuan for construction, as well as exempting it from taxes, in order to promote the use of national goods. (Special dispatch from the 15th)

Hubei Construction Department Inspects All Shipping Vessels

(Hankou) The Construction Department will escort all shipping vessels back to Wuhan for inspection and then allocate them to the Xiang, Chuan, Xiangwu, and other shipping routes to restore transportation. (Special dispatch from the 15th)

British Ambassador Cancels Trip to Chongqing

(Hankou) The British ambassador has canceled his trip to Chongqing and is scheduled to return to Nanjing and head north on the 16th. (Special dispatch from the 15th)

Corruption Case Discovered in the Hubei Special Tax Office

(Hankou) After the dismissal of Huang Zhenxing, Director of the Hubei Special Tax Office, a major corruption case was discovered, and many key members of the office are implicated. Huang's brother and Chen, Director of the Supervision Institute, have been arrested. The office will be reorganized into the Ten Provinces Tobacco Prohibition Supervisory Office. (Special dispatch from the 15th)

Lin Baek Leaves Hankou for Beiping

(Hankou) Lin Baek, advisor to the National Government, arrived in Hankou on the 14th and left for Beiping on the 15th. He is scheduled to return to the United States via Europe in October. Lin talked about his impressions of China, saying that Japan's manipulation of puppet organizations and seizure of Chinese land is no longer suitable for the modern era and will not benefit Japan in the future. He will return to the United States and urge the conclusion of a Sino-American reciprocal trade treaty to further strengthen Sino-American friendship. (Special dispatch from the 15th)

Chiang Tingwen to Host Banquet for Imamura Today

(Xiamen) After Imamura arrived in Xiamen, he visited Chiang Tingwen at noon on the 14th. Chiang returned the visit in the afternoon and scheduled a banquet for Imamura at noon on the 16th. Imamura is scheduled to leave Xiamen for Shantou that evening. The Third Fleet is responsible for the security of all of China. (Special dispatch from the 15th)

Sihai Steamer Tragedy

Bereaved Families Demand Compensation

(Guangzhou) Two weeks ago, the Sihai steamer sank in the Pearl River due to overcrowding, resulting in more than 300 casualties, making it the biggest tragedy in recent years. Today, relatives of the victims petitioned the government to immediately investigate the cause of the accident and punish port personnel for neglecting their duties and allowing overcrowding. At the same time, they demanded that the shipping company provide compensation of 5,000 yuan per person, totaling approximately 1.5 million yuan. (Reuters telegram from the 15th)

Guangzhou-Longzhou Route Test Flight Successful

(Guangzhou) The Southwest Aviation Company's aircraft recently completed successful test flights on the routes between Guangzhou and Longzhou, as well as Nanning and Guiyang. The aircraft took off from Guiyang yesterday and, weather permitting, will return to Guangzhou via Hainan Island. According to personnel from the Southwest Aviation Company today, the Guangzhou-Longzhou route will officially begin operations at the end of this month. (Reuters telegram from the 15th)

Silk Expert Mary Returns to Nanjing

(Hong Kong) Silk expert Mary completed her investigation in Guangdong and returned to Nanjing on the 15th to report on her findings. (Special dispatch from the 15th)

Hangzhou Plans to Issue Waterworks Bonds

(Hangzhou) Zhou Xiangxian, Mayor of Hangzhou, stated that the waterworks owes the city government a large sum of money, and the funds for municipal undertakings are insufficient. In order to implement various municipal construction projects, waterworks bonds with a face value of 2.5 million yuan will be issued, and the provincial government has approved the resolution. Preparations are currently underway. In addition, land value tax will also be thoroughly reorganized. (Central News Agency telegram from the 15th)

(Hangzhou) The Zhejiang Provincial Chamber of Commerce held a joint meeting of directors and supervisors at 3:00 p.m. on the 14th to elect a chairman due to the death of Chairman Wang Zhuzhai. Jiangxi Bandit Puppet 13th Division

Attempt to Counterattack Ends in Miserable Defeat

Scattered and Fled Towards Taihewei and Kangdu

Ji'an and Le'an Communist Suppression Teams Telegraph Province to Report Victory

Nanchang Correspondence, Nanfeng Report, Jiangxi East bandits, since being severely damaged by the National Army in the Lichuan Xiangfeng Xuangu'ao area, are eager for revenge. On the 4th of this month, the puppet 13th Division took advantage of the fact that Fan Wu's fortifications were not yet completed and launched a fierce counterattack against the positions of the 474th Regiment of the Third Route Army of the National Army. The puppet 38th Regiment restrained the supplementary regiment of the whole bamboo National Army, and the 37th and 39th Regiments attacked the left wing of the National Army at Guchenggang. The 9th Company of the 474th Regiment at Tongqianzhai immediately stopped working and calmly responded to the battle. The bandit forces were very stubborn. Fortunately, Zhang Xiting, the battalion commander of the 1st Battalion of the 474th Regiment, arrived with the 2nd and 3rd Companies, and the National Army's front line became more solid. The bandit forces repeatedly attacked the National Army's flank, but were all swept away by the National Army's machine guns and bombarded by mortars, coupled with the support of airplanes. The bandit puppet 37th Regiment suffered heavy casualties. At 4 p.m., the bandit puppet 39th Regiment continued to attack, and the 8th Company of the battalion quickly reinforced, and the supplementary regiment sent a battalion of troops to attack. By 7:30 p.m., the entire bandit puppet 13th Division had collapsed and scattered towards Taihewei and Kangdu. In this battle, the bandit forces suffered 700-800 casualties, more than 100 were captured, and dozens of guns were seized. The National Army suffered only 7 soldier casualties.

In addition, the Civil Affairs Department yesterday received reports from various counties on the situation of the Communist Suppression Volunteer Teams suppressing bandits: (1) Wen Huichou, magistrate of Ji'an County, reported that the Communist Suppression Volunteer Team of Tianhe, Ji'an County, advanced to suppress the puppet 8th District Guerrilla Team entrenched in Guoshui a few days ago. After contacting the bandits for about an hour, they killed more than ten bandits, seized three rifles, recruited five defectors, brought one rifle, and rescued more than 100 hostages. After the great victory, the Communist Suppression Volunteer Team took advantage of the victory and attacked the puppet village government and puppet short gun team puppet guerrilla team in Gaoche, Wutong, and Qingshi Township at dawn the next day. The bandit forces were unable to resist and fled towards Aocheng. Several bandits were captured on the spot, and many puppet seals and puppet propaganda materials were seized. (2) Zhang Xiangfu, magistrate of Le'an County, reported that more than 30 bandits were suddenly discovered in Xiqiliao, Xiangshanbei, Le'an County a few days ago. Dai Yuhe, deputy captain of the 3rd Brigade Communist Suppression Volunteer Team, led 50 team members and assisted the Special Operations Team to advance to suppress them in the evening of the same day. The place was full of steep cliffs and freezing cold. Each team proceeded at risk, wrapping their feet in rags. They arrived at the location at 10:00 p.m., waving flags and shouting, with great power and prestige. After a fierce battle of about an hour and a half, they finally defeated the bandit forces and immediately set fire to destroy the bandit den. In this battle, four bandits were killed, six bandits were captured, four rifles and twenty bullets were seized, and the remaining military supplies were collected by the Special Operations Team. (March 14)

He Chengjun

Setting Off to Suppress Bandits in Northern Hubei

To Convene a Meeting of Generals in Fancheng

Then Visit Guanghua, Yunxian, and Yunxian to Inspect Defense

Hankou Correspondence, Chairman Chiang, because the counties in northern Hubei border the three provinces of Henan, Shaanxi, and Sichuan, and the mountains are overlapping and stretch for thousands of miles, when the bandits of Xu Xiangqian, Wu Huanxian, and Liu Guitang were defeated, he feared that they would flee into the area, rely on the mountains to hide themselves, leading to prolonged military operations and no rest for the people. He specifically telegraphed He Chengjun, the pacification envoy stationed in Hubei, to set off for Xiangfan to take responsibility for overseeing the suppression. After receiving the order, He set off from Wuhan on the 10th, but the trip was postponed due to rain. It was not until this (14th) morning that he took the Hubei East Highway and transferred to the Xianghua Highway north. The accompanying personnel included Guan Linshu, Chief of Staff; Yang Duo, Section Chief; Xu Xuzhong, Staff Officer; Guan Wenhui; Wen Zhenfan, Adjutant; Liu Shiying; Ying Hong, Quartermaster; Zhou Jisheng, Secretary; Liu Danqi, Liu Jiahu, and Zhang Mingzhai, Telegraphers; and a platoon of escorts. They are scheduled to pass through Hanchuan and Yunmeng in the morning and transfer to Anlu at noon. If there are no delays, they will go directly to Xiangyang via Suixian and Zhaoyang, and temporarily reside in Fancheng within days. He will also convene Fan Shisheng, Zhang Zhenhan, Luo Qijiang, and other generals in Fancheng for a consultation to decide on a new plan, and then visit Guanghua, Yunxian, and Yunxian to inspect. He's mission to the north includes six tasks: (1) Supervising the various armies to eliminate the remnants of bandits on the border between Henan, Hubei, and Shaanxi; (2) Formulating a fundamental plan to prevent Xu's bandits; (2) Inspecting the bandit prevention bunkers in various counties; (4) Surveying the transportation on the borders of various provinces; (5) Examining the discipline of the various armies; (6) Inquiring about the sufferings of the people. After all, transportation in northern Hubei is blocked, the people are ignorant, and in military terms, it is an important town. It is necessary to make arrangements before the bandit tracks arrive. He said before leaving that he would set an entire plan for the scattered bandits in Xiangfan, order the garrison to search and suppress them, and set a time limit for elimination. Liu Guitang's remnant bandits were previously reported to have fled to Nanzhao and Nanyang. After failing to flee south, they have now fled east to the Pinghan Railway via Linying and are attempting to enter Shandong. The bandit has fled for thousands of miles and suffered heavy losses. There is little strength left, and it will not be difficult to wipe them out by encircling them. He will return to Hankou after inspecting northern Hubei, but the period cannot be predetermined. During He's departure period, the affairs of the Pacification Office will be handled by Yang Kuiyi, Chief of Staff; Zhu Chuanjing, Chief Advisor; and Chen Guangzu, Director of the Office, respectively. Important official affairs will be reported to the superiors for approval at any time. (March 14)
