Municipal Government

Establishing Dongjiadu Ferry

Privately Operated Ferry Still Allowed to Operate

The Municipal Government issued a notice yesterday, which reads: "Notice is hereby given that the Dongjiadu area is densely populated and commercially centered. More than 10,000 people travel to and from the other side of the river every day. The existing ferry is poorly equipped, time-consuming, and dangerous, causing great inconvenience to travelers. In the 17th year of the Republic, the Municipal Public Utility Bureau prepared a plan to establish the Dongjiadu Ferry for the safety and convenience of travelers in the area and submitted it to the Municipal Government for approval. Now, the Municipal Government has repeatedly received letters from the local Party Department and reports from the industrial, commercial, and academic circles, requesting that the ferry be opened as soon as possible. The Mayor has observed the situation and believes that the ferry is indeed urgent. The ferry has been ordered to actively prepare according to the approved plan and open the ferry on schedule to facilitate transportation and comfort the people. The existing privately operated ferry in the area will still be allowed to operate after the municipal ferry is opened to show consideration. This notice is hereby given to all."

Mishandling of Gun Causes Accident

Xu Kou Fires Bullet Through Side of Nose

Xu Koufa, a 16-year-old native of Zhenjiang, works as an apprentice in the Jiangnan Shoe Store at the end of North Henan Road. A relative named Xu Xiangbing works as a clerk in the writing room at the North Railway Station (and lives at No. 7 Qingchang Lane, Avenue Eduard VII). Xu Xiangbing is a volunteer member of the Shanghai North Security Regiment, so he has a handgun, which he keeps in the desk in the writing room. Last night, Koufa and Xiangbing's younger brother, Xiangxi, went to visit Xiangbing. They happened to see a handgun and took it out to play with. Unexpectedly, there was still a bullet in the barrel. It fired at the slightest touch, hitting Koufa's left nostril. The bullet exited near the back of his ear, and he bled profusely and fainted to the ground. He was later taken to Renji Hospital for treatment.

Theft at Blue Funnel Wharf

Ten Cases of Serge, Worth 10,000 Yuan

When the Blue Funnel Wharf at Jiajiajiao, Pudong, opened its warehouse yesterday morning, it was discovered that goods worth more than 10,000 yuan were stolen from warehouse "E". The thieves seemed to have been hiding in the warehouse in advance. When everyone was asleep, they chiseled through the eight-inch cement floor in the southeast corner of the warehouse where white rattan was piled up, creating a round hole about fifteen inches in diameter. Two-Route Administration

Promoting Spring Travel

Dispatching Personnel to Greet Passengers for Convenience

Reducing Fares and Arranging Hotel Reservations

The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administrations, in order to promote spring travel,

specially established convenient travel measures, printed booklets, and distributed them to all sectors. The details are as follows:

Reasons for Promotion: "In the third month of late spring, the grasses grow tall in Jiangnan, miscellaneous flowers bloom on trees, and groups of orioles fly about." These sentences praising the spring scenery of Jiangnan can give an idea of Jiangnan's beauty in the spring. The areas passed through by these two routes, such as Nanjing, Zhenjiang, Suzhou, Wuxi, Hangzhou, etc., are all scenic spots in Jiangnan. Miscellaneous flowers and groups of orioles can be enjoyed everywhere. There are also outstanding mountains and rivers, and in recent years, many modern constructions have been added, which can supplement the shortcomings of nature. In such bright spring sunshine, touring beautiful places is truly a good way to regulate life. Moreover, the physical constitution of Chinese people is relatively weak, and the living environment tends to be static, so we are promoting travel and sightseeing, and formulating various measures to make travelers feel convenient everywhere.

Convenient Measures: A. Vehicle Transportation: Whether it is a group or an individual, in Nanjing, Shanghai, and Hangzhou, if you need to hire a car, rickshaw, or horse-drawn carriage, you only need to notify this route in advance, and you can hire from the agreed-upon car company. The car fare is the same as the market price. B. Dispatching Personnel to Greet: If you need guidance on sightseeing along the route when traveling on the two routes, you can contact the stations and business offices of this route, and we will dispatch familiar and capable staff to accompany you along the way, take care of everything, and guide you to various places of interest. C. Hotel Reservations: This route has many pre-booked room contracts with large and small hotels in Nanjing, Zhenjiang, Wuxi, Suzhou, Hangzhou, etc. Ordinary passengers, if they purchase tickets at the business office of this route, can entrust the business office to book in advance, which can greatly facilitate them. D. Fare Reduction: (1) Student groups of ten or more people will be charged 75% of the ordinary original price for one-way tickets and 50% for round-trip tickets (after the ticket price is reduced, the minimum price per person is 50 cents). (2) The fare reduction method for ordinary round-trip tickets is 75% of the ordinary fare for first class, 75% of the ordinary fare for second class, and 85% of the ordinary fare for third class. Special express surcharges will be charged in full.

Guangfeng Company

Robbery Case Involving Over 20,000 Yuan Solved

Instigated by a Laid-Off Cook

Three Criminals Arrested and Handed Over to the Authorities

The case of the North-South Distribution Office of Guangfeng Company, located at No. 11 Hengxing West Lane, Limah Road, 16th Pier, Nanshi, Shanghai, being robbed of 20,600 yuan in cash at 7:20 p.m. on February 4th of this year has been solved. It is learned that Detective Leader Dong Mingde, stationed in District 1 of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, discovered that it was instigated by Zhou Xiaotao from Tongzhou, the laid-off cook of the company. He had colluded with accomplices nicknamed "Living Monkey" Lin Gen, "Little Pockmark" Bao Azhang, and A Lin. After reporting the preliminary information to Team Leader Lu and District Chief Guan, Deputy Leader Han Ruisheng was dispatched to lead detectives and police officers to arrest the suspect Jin Qilang from Chongming, a cart puller, in Chunsen Lumber Company on Anlan Road, Xiaoximen, at 3 p.m. the day before yesterday. During the interrogation, Jin confessed, "I only know Zhou Xiaotao. I went to Pinfang Photo Studio in Chenghuang Temple to take pictures, but I don't know about the robbery. However, Zhou and Bao Azhang from Ningbo, who lives at No. 198 Danfeng Road, Xiaodongmen, are very close." According to the confession, Leader Dong immediately dispatched the original team of detectives and police officers from the Second Precinct of District 1 to Bao's house, arrested Bao, and took him to the district. Bao confessed that he met Zhou Xiaotao in August of last year, so Zhou often came to my house to play and chat. At the beginning of September, Zhou discussed with "Little Pockmark" about hating the boss for stopping business and wanting to rob him. He asked "Little Pockmark" if he had connections and if he was confident that the company had about 20,000 yuan. So, they discussed this matter at the end of September and again at the end of October. Lin Gen, nicknamed "Monkey," and A Rong joined them, totaling five people. They decided to buy five pistols in Suzhou and robbed the company on the evening of February 4th. On the 9th, "Little Pockmark" distributed 100 yuan in stolen money to me through Zhou Xiaotao, who is still at large. Lin Gen, the "Monkey," skimmed off 20 yuan, so I only got 80 yuan. Also, on the seventh day of the first lunar month, Zhang Mingfu (aka Blind Man), a carpenter from Changzhou who lives at No. 5, Alley 2, Danfeng Road, cheated me out of 6 yuan." The officers continued to arrest Zhang Mingfu the day before yesterday, bringing the total number of suspects to three. They were all handed over to the Third Division of the General Bureau yesterday morning for legal action.

Continued Interrogation of Suspects in the Tang Jiapeng Assassination Case

The case of Tang Jiapeng, the former manager of Rongji Amusement Park in the Great World, being assassinated on June 18th of last year has been investigated. The French Concession police arrested the suspects Zhang Xiaosizi (aka Zhang Tinggui) from Funing and Zhao Guangfu from Yangzhou, and confiscated a pistol. After comparing it with the bullet casings found at the scene, it was confirmed that three bullets were fired from this gun. They were handed over to the Second Special District Court for prosecution. Zhao was sentenced to life imprisonment, and Zhang was sentenced to 20 years of imprisonment. The two convicts refused to accept the judgment and appealed to the Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. Details have been reported in previous newspapers. The afternoon before yesterday, Chief Judge Guo of the High Court, along with Judges Fan and Sun, and Chief Prosecutor Zhao, opened the court for trial and appointed lawyer Wang Hengyi to defend the appellants. According to the reasons for dissatisfaction stated by Zhang and Zhao, they both denied knowing anything and claimed that they did not commit the murder and were arrested unjustly, requesting a retrial. However, they did not provide any solid evidence to the contrary. The court ordered a new trial at a later date, and the appellants were still detained pending further instructions.

National Hero at the Rongji Gong Stage

Meeting the People of This City Tonight

"Xue Rengui Settles Tianshan with Three Arrows" is one of the greatest national heroes in our country's history. At this time of serious national crisis, we should perform more plays about famous ancient generals with outstanding martial arts to awaken the patriotic spirit of the people. The Rongji Gong Stage in this city has newly arranged a play about Xue Rengui, using official history as the warp and folk legends as the weft. The first part starts with the Eastern Qi Kingdom offering tribute to Goryeo and Gai Suwen robbing treasures, and ends with Xue Rengui entrusting Liang and exchanging halberds and subduing the three bandits of Fenghuoshan. Dramas that combine history and patriotism are prone to being dry and boring, but this play is full of interest. From beginning to end, there is no dull scene. It is named a historical drama, but it combines heroism, romance, chivalry, and sorrow in one furnace. Such a good play is rare in our country's theaters. The stage spared no expense to specially produce multiple exquisite sets, which change rapidly and are wonderfully unpredictable. They are brilliantly dazzling and can be called a spectacle. It is said that the premiere is scheduled for tonight.

Reading Q&A

Further Discussion on Literary

Study Steps

Writing and Others

—A General Response to Messrs. Zhang Yiyan, Wu Kexun, Pan Fengshi, Ji Li, Cheng Tiesheng, Zheng Guoqin, et al.

We had a general discussion not long ago on the question of how to study literature. Now, because many readers are still writing in, requesting a clearer and more specific answer to this question, we are providing a few more opinions as a general response.

According to many letters, we see that in the minds of most people studying literature, there are three most basic problems that are considered urgent to solve: (1) What is the literature we need? (2) How to read literary books? (3) How to create? These three questions, if viewed together, can also be said to be the steps in studying literature.

(1) What is the literature we need? When we begin to study literature, the first difficulty we encounter is seeing the vast number of literary books, and not knowing where to start. In fact, there is no need to worry about this. If we have correct answers to the two prerequisite questions: "Why study literature?" and "What is the literature we need?", then the difficulty will be easily overcome. We know that literature is no longer just something for men of letters to enjoy, but something that expresses the complexity of a specific social life through images (words). Literature can expose the evils of a society, literature can depict the progress of a new society, and literature can enhance the interest in human life. The artistic value of literature is estimated in conjunction with its social value; that is to say, the literature of a certain era is most valuable at that time, and after that era, its value will inevitably decrease. From this point of view, it is clear that we study literature not for entertainment, nor solely to learn some writing skills, but because we want to understand the truth of the social activities we are in from within literary works; from within literary works, we want to obtain information for our current lives. Thus, the literature we need is undoubtedly the work that best fits the current society, and is most capable of shouting out the pain of our current lives and pointing out the course of life. Some people suggest reading *Guwen Guanzhi* ("Anthology of Ancient Prose"), our answer is: *Guwen Guanzhi* is definitely not what we need. Old Chinese literature, in coordination with the decline of Chinese society into a semi-feudal state, is always circling within forms. What it leaves us is only the remains of those forms. Ask: which of the essays of the Eight Great Prose Masters of the Tang and Song dynasties has anything to do with our current society and life? Moreover, the editors of *Guwen Guanzhi* forcibly divide the structure of each article into "beginning, development, transition, and conclusion," making it rigid. Even if you want to study ancient prose, or want to learn some writing skills from it, this is not a very good anthology of ancient prose. Secondly, some people suggest reading *Dream of the Red Chamber*. Our answer is, likewise, that it is not needed. *Dream of the Red Chamber* is indeed a valuable literary work, but its value lies in the fact that it can comprehensively and intricately express the licentious life of the declining aristocracy at that time. Now, society has changed, and what has replaced the aristocracy are warlords and bureaucrats. Their licentiousness and brutality are no longer as depicted in *Dream of the Red Chamber*, but have taken on a new guise. In this way, what *Dream of the Red Chamber* gives us is only sexual stimulation and temptation. We are not like young masters and misses who have leisure and elegance, so how can we have the mood to enjoy that sensual entertainment? In addition, chivalrous novels and boring triangular or quadrangular love novels that are currently popular are all unnecessary. Chivalrous novels intentionally avoid real society and lead people to think wildly. Current society is evil, and to transform this society, each basic active cell of society—that is, we ourselves who suffer the most—must take responsibility. But what chivalrous novels tell us is to wait for those heroes with chivalrous hearts and the ability to swallow bullets and spit out swords to save us. That kind of hero will never exist in the world, so we can only be forever mired in groaning and pain. This is a deception, a kind of anesthesia! As for boring love novels, although their form of expression is different from chivalrous novels, their function is no different. It does not avoid reality but distorts reality, attempting to use sexual stimulation to soften the pain we suffer, to ease our criticism of current society, and thus to block our way to survival. Ask: in our difficult lives, why should we waste time and energy reading literary works that are useless and greatly harmful to us?

As mentioned earlier, the literature we need must be the literature that vividly depicts the complexity and richness of life, under the source of progress in current society, within the key to affirmation and negation. We read "The True Story of Ah Q" because "The True Story of Ah Q" not only depicts a typical peasant figure in the early Chinese revolution, but also depicts the overall face of Chinese society, which is mired in a semi-feudal state. We read "Midnight" because "Midnight" indicates the inevitable collapse of Chinese industrial capital under the double attack of rural bankruptcy and imperialist dumping. However, what we should pay attention to here is that in our China, which has a low level of culture, and where new culture has not yet had sufficient opportunity to develop, the readable literary works that are relatively rich in social significance are still extremely scarce. Therefore, we cannot but rely on those great works translated from foreign countries. (Of course, many foreign works are also boring.) From the present point of view, the field of literature has no national boundaries, just as China can no longer close itself off. We can no longer harbor prejudice, and no longer fear the demise of old Chinese literature. Those who see it that way are merely trying to exert their share of power to hinder the development of new culture. Having recognized these, we should no longer find it difficult to choose literary books to read. (Regarding the books that should be read, we plan to provide a more detailed book list in the future, so we will not go into detail here.)

Next, we will talk about how to read literary books.

Spring and Autumn

Anecdotes About Eating

— Zhanlu

The conversation at spring banquets often "talks about eating," discussing many anecdotes about eating. There is an old Mr. Pan with a beard that reaches his abdomen, who has traveled half of China and is familiar with anecdotes about eating. The following "history of gluttony" is what he told while laughing and stroking his beard: During the Qianlong reign, the Grand Strategist Fukang'an was a gluttony expert; when state and county officials were handling his affairs, everyone shook their heads. One day, Grand Strategist Fu passed by a certain county. Knowing that this was a barren county, he was particularly considerate and did not ask the county magistrate to prepare a full table of dishes, only "boiled pork" would suffice.

Boiled pork is a very common dish that does not cost much money. The county magistrate was relieved to hear these instructions and was about to order the kitchen to prepare it accordingly. However, he was informed by Grand Strategist's entourage that there was no need for the county magistrate to prepare it. He only needed to present fat pigs, and Grand Strategist's own cooks would know how to prepare it according to the law. The county magistrate thought that one fat pig would be enough for one meal of boiled pork. However, Grand Strategist's entourage demanded fifty fat pigs, which was the minimum limit, and not one could be missing. The county magistrate had to requisition fifty fat pigs everywhere and send them to the Grand Commissioner's residence to prepare for Grand Strategist Fu's meal of boiled pork.

The county magistrate was curious in his heart, why would so many fat pigs be needed for one meal of boiled pork? When it was time for Grand Strategist's lunch, he went to the residence very respectfully to take care of things. The so-called taking care of things was actually to see how the boiled pork made from these fifty fat pigs was prepared. He saw that there were many small dishes on the table, mostly salty, spicy, sour, and sweet, which were prepared for dipping the boiled pork in. After everything was arranged, the cooks carried two large basins stacked with boiled pork that was about a foot high to the table. This kind of boiled pork was simply unheard of. Each piece was as round as the seasonal spring pancakes on the market, with fat meat around the circumference and lean meat in the middle, stacked layer upon layer, with no difference in the surroundings. How was it made? After Grand Strategist Fu had a full meal, he took his entourage to another place.

After the imperial envoy left, the county magistrate went to visit the kitchen near the residence and heard a series of pig's screams. It turned out that the fifty fat pigs were struggling in a pool of blood. Only four pieces of hip meat were cut from each fat pig, and the two pieces on the surface were not used. The hip meat cut from the second knife was used, so the circumference was fat, and the center was lean.

Fukang'an, who had a full meal, went far away, and five hundred fat pigs without buttocks were still wailing in the pool—

Anecdotes of Wu Zhiying

— Qingqu

Wu Zhiying, the wife of Lian Nanhu, is now heard to have passed away due to illness. She was a senior member of the women's circle, another weakened, which is very deplorable. Therefore, I will describe one or two anecdotes to inform the readers. Madam is the niece of Mr. Wu Zhipu of Tongcheng. Her father's name was Baoshan, and he was a county magistrate in a certain county in Shandong. He had the reputation of being a good official and was quite known for his political achievements. Madam had no younger siblings and was doted on as a child. Although she was a talented woman, she was treated no differently than a son. As she grew up, she became proficient in classics and history, and was especially good at calligraphy. She was slender and graceful, and was treasured by the literati. She had indeed obtained the legacy of Madam Wei.

Lian Nanhu of Wuxi was a director in the Ministry of Revenue during the late Qing Dynasty. Madam was with him there, and almost all the dignitaries in Beijing knew Madam's name. Empress Dowager Cixi admired her calligraphy and was able to enjoy rewards together with Yu Shenshou's exquisite embroidery, which was called a momentary competition. At that time, Liu Tieyun had a stele inscription in his collection, which was a legal treasure rarely seen in the world. However, Madam wanted him to part with it, and they fought over it for many years without success, eventually leading to a rift. This was spread as a good story in the capital. When Nanhu resigned and returned to the south, he built a villa in the western suburbs of Shanghai, calling his residence "Wanliu Caotang" ("Ten Thousand Willow Thatched Cottage"). Among the weeping willows, the scenery was superb. Madam called herself "Madam Wanliu" ("Madam Ten Thousand Willow"), and was inseparable from the famous courtesan Li Pingxiang. Because Pingxiang was good at chanting, their communication became closer and closer, to the point of not hesitating to remove her hairpins and earrings to redeem her from her registration. Her chivalry and love for talent were something that even men could not match. When Qiu Jin's case of being beheaded in Tinglin arose, Madam exerted herself to help, but to no avail. She and Xu Jichen and others finally buried her bones at the foot of West Lake, and erected a stele to inscribe it. Not long after, Chang Hui, an official of the Censorate, heard about it and sent a memorial to impeach her, so her tomb was cut down. Madam relied on the strength of the female missionary Mai Meide to escape by luck. By the time of the Xinhai Revolution, the righteous voice rose in Hubei. From then on, she was reburied in Xiling, and thousands of people in Shanghai held ropes to help carry the coffin. They used noodles to make extremely large turtles resembling Zhang Zengzhi, the governor of Zhejiang, and Gui Fu, the prefect of Shaoxing, and followed them in the procession, all because of Madam's fight.

Madam wrote a copy of the Surangama Sutra, which was extremely valuable. She said of herself, "Today, there are many fleshy eyes, and no one can recognize it. In five hundred years, they should appreciate it between the writing brush and the ink." She wanted to build a seven-level pagoda as a foundation for the Sutra, but she never succeeded. Now, Madam's lifetime of handwriting, I don't know where it has fallen.

Change

— Qian Zuizhu

With a creak, the door suddenly opened. The dispirited Jiying came jumping into my room with a letter in his hand. He kept shouting:

"Linbo's letter is here! Linbo's letter is here!" I was startled by him! Looking at his face, some joy was revealed in his tightly knit brows! A hint of red light also appeared on his haggard forehead.

"What does Linbo's letter say?"

I asked faintly, knowing that this was not good news.

"He is waiting for me in Dalian to go to Kuanchengzi together. If the travel expenses are not enough, he told me to ask Zhang Guojie in Tianjin for them."

Jiying told me loudly and happily.

"Zhang Guojun? Isn't that the guy Touyama Matajiro?"

Perhaps my tone was a little serious, making Jiying a little hesitant:

"Yes...yes...it's him, but...I for..."

Jiying discovered some embarrassment.

"No matter what for? I don't think you have reached the point of selling yourself to rely on others..."

My words were not finished, and Jiying became angry!

"What do you mean by selling myself to rely on others? That's too disrespectful!"

"Yes! My words are a little straightforward: but please forgive my personality."

"You only care about your personality, and don't care about people's faces, lives, and each person has his own aspirations, goodbye."

Jiying left with a bang, venting his angry attitude.

Jiying is gone! And I, immersed in sad reveries, couldn't help but want to cry!

Three years ago, Jiying, who was on the seat of the student union representative, was what kind of person? And what kind of person is he now? Who made him change like this? Alas!

Complaining About the Job You're In

— Jiang Liusheng

After reading Mr. Zhang Bingduo's article "Literati" in the Japanese section, I couldn't help but express a lot of sympathy. Two or three years ago, I was also a person who buried myself in paperwork all day long, writing non-stop in what is called a writing career. Later, because the life of a literati was too miserable and too pitiful, they even died from overwork. No one even felt sorry for them, and they were sometimes ridiculed and sarcastically given a eulogy of "not worth dying for" if they were given a little condolence money. So, I was determined to throw away my bald brush, become a monk halfway, and change my career to the advertising industry. Before I knew it, I had been mixed up for more than two years. Although I was much more comfortable and smooth in terms of economic and spiritual aspects, sometimes I still felt the pain of being at the mercy of others and swallowing my anger. As the saying goes, "complaining about the job you're in" is indeed true.

I can hear the tone of complaint and lamentation in teahouses and restaurants at any time. How someone is suffering, how someone is complaining about their fate, and in A's case, they always think that if they reach B's position, they will definitely be comfortable and avoid pain. When A really reaches B's position, A will complain again and again, just like before.

Alas! It is human nature to like the new and dislike the old, but unfortunately, the self-selection of occupations and the change of positions cannot be as desired. No wonder warlords, politicians, great men, and celebrities want to fight each other and seize power. (However, this is a reward)

Research on Inkstones (3)

— Wuliaoke

(II) The trend of pragmatism to artistic inclination

Why does the practical inkstone gradually tend towards artistic inclination? The reason is very simple: First, Chinese people are rich in elegant and noble entertainment. "If a workman wants to do his job well, he must first sharpen his tools" is an ancient motto. The tools that literary, calligraphy, and painting masters of the past have relied on are the four treasures of the study. Among the four treasures, inkstones are especially valued. The ancients said that brushes live for days, ink lives for months, and inkstones live for generations. The intention is clear. It is also said: bright windows and clean desks, fine brushes and ink, are the pleasures of literati. Inkstones should also be included. Since people love their inkstones, they spare no effort to think and research each item to express its beauty, so the size, style, carving, inscription, and material style of the inkstone box also progress with the progress of literature and art, and change with the changes of the times and tastes. Therefore, it is not unfounded to say that the inkstone is sufficient to represent the art and literature of the times. Second, the trend of loving inkstones was initiated in the imperial palaces, and the literary attendants echoed it, so the trend spread extremely easily. Chinese art and literature gradually began to develop after the Qin and Han dynasties. At that time, inkstones were very simple. The concave inkstones that were popular in the Jin dynasty, and the later human-faced inkstones and Phoenix Pool basket-shaped inkstones, were already novel and special, but their production was also simple. For example, the inkstones carved by Wang Xizhi, Wang Xianzhi, and Gu Kaizhi, as seen in the spectrum, are very few. By the early Tang dynasty, Emperor Taizong and Emperor Gaozong promoted culture at the top, and literary figures, calligraphers, and painters such as Yu Shinan, Ouyang Xun, Chu Suiliang, Wu Daozi, Wang Wei, Yan Zhenqing, etc., emerged one after another. Therefore, the production style of inkstones gradually changed and improved. It was necessary to be appropriate and suitable for use, and to seek fine and pleasing workmanship. The patterns gradually increased. In the late Tang dynasty, the carving on the side of the inkstone became popular, and the carving method changed. Zhao Song, which rose three hundred years after the Tang dynasty, re-promoted and carried forward culture. There were many scholars who were proficient in poetry, prose, and painting, so the carving of inkstones became more and more beautiful. According to Du Wan's Yunlin Stone Spectrum, there are more than seventy styles of inkstones. Shang Sisun's Inkstone Note's inkstone illustration says that there are twenty-four kinds of inkstones that are close to elegance, as follows:

Phoenix Pool, Jade Hall, Jade Terrace, Penglai, Biyong, Academy style, Fang Xiang style, Langguan style, Sky Inkstone, Wind character, Human face, Gui, Bi, Axe, Tripod, Ding, Yuqu

Curved water, Eight edges, Four straight, Lotus leaf, Toad, Horse hoof

According to the inkstone illustrations on Wenfang Sicao, in addition to the above twenty-four kinds, there are also basket styles, melon styles, fairy peach styles, bell styles, egg styles, turtle styles, shuttle styles, zither styles, pipa styles, double fish styles, group styles, moon styles, waist drum styles, moon pool styles, etc. As for the wind-character style, there are so-called draped skirt wind characters, flat-bottom wind characters, footed wind characters, ancient style wind characters, zither-footed wind characters (and it is explained that the Xuanhe reign period's imperial government descended in style, the shape is like a wind character, such as the Phoenix Pool style, but there are four rings carved with seawater fish and dragon three sacred mountains and water pools made in the shape of Kunlun, with the left sun and right moon stars arranged to supply the Supreme Emperor's book office), and the four straight styles have so-called ancient style four straight, double brocade four straight, Hehuan four straight. The eight-edged styles have so-called eight-edged corner handle held inkstones, eight-edged held inkstones, bamboo joint held inkstones. There are even more names. The Song dynasty inkstone style, recorded in Tang Jizhi's Shezhou Inkstone Spectrum, also occasionally differs. In short, this kind of inkstone style change probably originated in the palace, which can be believed.

Four Northeast Company Commanders

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Twenty-Five

Tearful Faces Send People Away from Home to Distant Garrison

Wind and Sand All Night Long Go Out of the Fortress to Station in a Lonely City

Shili stood outside laughing and shouting; don't sleep, there are guests coming to the fort. The person inside heard an unfamiliar voice and asked several times who it was. Everyone followed the loess wall and saw two closed sorghum doors with two red square pieces of paper with the character "喜" ("happiness") written on them. This kind of thing shot into Ziqiang's eyes and made his heart move involuntarily. Looking at the red paper again, it was still unusually bright, clearly posted not long ago. Ziqiang stared blankly and hadn't said a word yet. The two sorghum doors were pulled open, and a middle-aged man came out, wearing a blue cloth cotton robe and a blue cloth mandarin jacket. Although the people outside the pass don't know how to comb that artistic hair, the duck-butt style combed on the back half of the head is jet black and shiny, which is clearly the bridegroom. He saw four soldiers and stammered early: old old...general, ask ask...who? While speaking, his eyes turned and his body kept retreating. Ziqiang waved his hand and said: Don't be afraid, we are here to talk to the fort director here, please tell me where he lives? Before he could answer, a woman shouted: Run for your life, big...big soldiers are coming tens of thousands of them. This shout caused the dogs in the fort to bark, and people came out of each loess house. Ziqiang knew very well that the people of Rehe Province had suffered from the harassment of the local bandit-turned-soldiers, so they were frightened out of their wits when they saw the soldiers coming. He had to stand in the center of the village house, waving his hands and shouting not to be afraid, not to be afraid. But he had been blown by the wind and sand all night, and his face was stained with wind and sand like Zhang Fei, and even his nose and eyes could not be distinguished. The gray uniform on his body had become half black, and the yellow mud on his feet was level with his trouser legs. Even without weapons on his body, he was a living ghost, let alone that he had a pistol and the people who followed him each carried a rifle, which was even more terrifying. He opened his mouth, revealing white teeth on his black face. Everyone could only see him getting anxious, and couldn't hear what he was saying. The more he waved and shouted, the more people ran away. (337)

Zhejiang Province's Primary School Funding Standards for Each County and City

The Zhejiang Education Department believes that the primary school funding standards for each county and city in the province have not yet been uniformly stipulated, and it is temporarily difficult to promote assessment. Therefore, based on the actual situation of each county and city, it has formulated eight standards and has been approved by the Ministry of Education for record. Yesterday, it issued orders to the county and city governments to comply with them. The original text is as follows: Article 1: These standards are based on Article 22 of the Primary School Regulations. Article 2: The start-up costs of primary schools in each county and city shall be handled in accordance with the provisions of Article 20 of the Primary School Regulations. Article 3: The regular expenses of public primary schools in each county and city for each grade in each academic year shall be budgeted in accordance with the minimum standard numbers stipulated in the following table according to the different structures and grades.

Article 6: The distribution of regular expenses for primary schools in each county and city shall be handled in accordance with the provisions of Article 21 of the Primary School Regulations. Article 7: If any county or city has special difficulties in educational funding and cannot handle matters in accordance with these standards, it may separately formulate standards and submit them to the Provincial Education Department for approval before implementation. National

The History of Private Independent Colleges

The Ministry of Education has compiled the following history of private independent colleges across the country: 1. Hackett Medical College was initially named Guangdong Women's Medical School, founded by American doctor Mary H. Fulton. Later, due to donor relationships, it was once named Sangji Hospital, Rouji Pharmacy School, and Duan Nai Nursing School. Seven years before the Republic (of China), it was renamed Hackett Medical University because Hackett's donations were the largest. In the 14th year of the Republic, it was changed to its current name, and in December of the 21st year, it was approved for registration. 2. Xiehe Medical College was initially named Xiehe Medical College, jointly established by five groups of churches from the United Kingdom and the United States, and the London Medical Society. In the 4th year of the Republic, it was taken over by the Rockefeller Foundation's China Medical Board and renamed Xiehe Medical University. In the 18th year, it was renamed Private Peking Union Medical College in accordance with the Ministry's order. 3. Zhijiang College of Arts and Sciences: The school was initially named Chongxin Yishu, later changed to Yuying Yishu, Yuying Academy. One year before the Republic, the Southern Presbyterian Church joined in preparing for the university, named after the river. It ceased operation in the 17th year due to a lack of leadership, resumed in the spring of the 18th year, and was approved for registration by the Ministry in July of the 20th year. 4. Jiaozuo Institute of Technology was initially named Jiaozuo Railway and Mining School, closed in the first year of the Republic, changed to Fuzhong Mining School in the fourth year, changed to a specialized school in the eighth year, changed to a university in the tenth year, recognized by the former Ministry of Education in the 16th year, changed to its current name in April of the 20th year, and provisionally approved for registration in July of the 21st year. 5. China College was initially named National University. In the third year, it was merged with Wusong China Public School and renamed the University Department of China Public School. In March of the sixth year, it separated from the Public School, renamed China University. In October of the 19th year, it was changed to its current name and approved for registration by the Ministry. 6. Chaoyang College was initially named Beijing Private National University, recognized by the former Ministry of Education in May of the third year. In February of the fifth year, it was renamed Chaoyang University. In November of the 19th year, it was approved for registration by the Ministry and changed to its current name. 7. Xiangya Medical College was initially named Specialized School, jointly established by Hunan Qunxue Society and Yale-in-China, with records filed with the former Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Internal Affairs, and Finance, and the Hunan Provincial Government. The contract expired in the 13th year and was renewed for ten years, renamed Xiangya Medical University. It was closed in the spring of the 16th year due to a political upheaval. The current school was reorganized in the 18th year. In December of the 20th year, it was approved for registration by the Ministry. 8. Ginling College was founded by the church, initially named Ginling Women's University. In the 14th year of the Republic, the physical education normal school run by the Young Women's Christian Association (YWCA) was merged into it. In November of the 19th year, it was approved for registration by the Ministry and changed to its current name. 9. Fukien Christian College was initially named Fukien Christian University, founded by the International Missionary Alliance. In January of the 20th year of the Republic, it was approved for registration by the Ministry and changed to its current name. 10. Minguo College was initially Minguo University, founded by Zhang Ji and others, reorganized and established in April of the sixth year, approved for registration successively by the former Ministries of Education, Agriculture, and Justice in the 11th year. In January of the 19th year, it was provisionally approved for registration by the Ministry and renamed to its current name. 11. China Public School was transformed and upgraded from the previously closed China Public School. In August of the 15th year, it was recognized by the former Ministry of Education. In June of the 19th year, it was approved for registration by the Ministry. In February of the 20th year, the Ministry dispatched personnel to take over due to an incident, and in March, it was handed over to the new principal. The Ministry ordered it to be closed down gradually due to the damage caused by the Shanghai war, until all students graduated. 12. North China College was initially North China University, approved for registration by the former Ministry of Education and the Ministry of Justice in the 13th year. In August of the 20th year, it was submitted to the Ministry for approval for registration. 13. Shanghai College of Law and Politics was initially named Shanghai College of Law and Politics. In the summer of the 16th year, it was sealed up by the government due to political reasons. It was later reopened, approved for registration by the Ministry in June of the 19th year, and renamed to its current name. 14. Chih Chih College was founded by He Shizhen and others, prepared in the 13th year, and officially opened in the 14th year. In July of the 20th year, it was approved for registration by the Ministry. 15. Shanghai Law College was initially named Shanghai Law University. In January of the 19th year, it was changed to Shanghai Law College. In June of the same year, it was approved for registration by the Ministry. The school buildings were destroyed in the Shanghai war, and it moved to Hangzhou to open. It moved back to Shanghai in September. 16. Nantong College was initially the agricultural science, medical science (established six years before the Republic), and textile science (established in the first year of the Republic) colleges founded by the Zhang Jian brothers of Nantong. In the 17th year, the three schools were merged into Nantong University. In August of the 19th year, it was approved by the Ministry to be renamed to its current name. 17. Zhengfeng College of Arts was originally named Zhengfeng University of Arts. In the 18th year, it was changed to Zhengfeng College of Arts. In August of the 21st year, it was provisionally approved for registration by the Ministry. 18. Fujian College was founded by Yang Shuzhuang. In July of the 21st year, it was provisionally approved for registration by the Ministry.

Education Associations of Various Counties

Request Jiangsu Provincial Government to Maintain Education Funds

Local Budget Meeting Resolutions Hinder Education

Jiading County Education Association telegraphed yesterday requesting exemption from reduction

The Jiangsu Finance Department previously held a local budget meeting, preparing to implement tax cuts starting from the 23rd year. Although it stated that education funds would not be reduced, according to reliable sources, a certain section chief of the Education Department strongly argued with the provincial government about this matter to the point of resigning but was unsuccessful, indicating the seriousness of the situation. The Shanghai County Education Association had previously telegraphed the Ministry of Education and the provincial government to appeal. Yesterday, the Jiading County Education Association also telegraphed the provincial government and the Education Department, strongly requesting exemption from reduction. The original telegram is recorded as follows: To Chairman Chen and Director Zhou Jun of the Zhenjiang Provincial Government and the Education Department, respectively: Our Jiangsu Province has long been known as a land of culture. According to recent statistics, there are 4,620,536 school-age children in the province, while only 624,240 children are enrolled in school. The number of out-of-school children reaches over 85 percent. Given the urgency of foreign aggression and the perilous state of the nation, we should focus all our efforts on school education, which is the foundation of the nation, and fully expand local education funds, which are the lifeblood of education, to plan for the long-term cultivation of talent and to seek a way for national survival. However, since the restriction of land tax to 101 yuan and the regulation of 1.6 jiao per mu, it has become a pie in the sky, and the door to opening up sources of education funds has been blocked. As a result, the plans of various counties to actively expand education have become fantasies. From then on, no matter how well-thought-out and proactive the administrators of Jiangsu education are, they will find it difficult to escape the scope of maintaining the status quo. Moreover, there are even more cases where counties, due to famine, war, and the short collection of fixed expenses, have accumulated debts and cannot even maintain the status quo. Recently, the Finance Department held a local budget meeting for the 22nd year, and again allocated 20 percent of the autumn survey's actual tax revenue as the general reserve fund for various undertakings in the county, in preparation for tax cuts in the 23rd year. This method has already been clearly announced in the instruction to the Changshu County Government on January 22nd. This association previously believed that education funding was insufficient, but hoped that a good harvest and the absence of war would make it easier to gradually increase it. Now, not only is there no hope of increasing it, but the move to reduce it is being prepared for implementation. Witnessing this, we find it difficult to remain silent. The collection of taxes is borne by the people, and the education funds collected from the people are still used for the benefit of the people. Investing one cent of money today will yield ten times the results in the future, which cannot be compared to other passive expenses. Therefore, even if it is slightly heavy, it is not considered harsh. Moreover, the amount collected per mu is extremely small, and even if the people's strength is exhausted, they would not be unable to bear this trivial amount. However, when accumulated, it will have a great impact on the education of the entire province. If education funds are actually reduced, the current state of education in various counties will be impossible to maintain, and what was once known for its cultural development will turn into educational bankruptcy. Tracing the origin and entrusting the matter in detail, who will bear this heavy responsibility and blame? We dare to telegraph Your Honor to request that you exempt the reduction of local education funds, which are the lifeblood of education, in order to maintain the status quo and avoid bankruptcy. The telegram is urgently sent, and we hope that you will graciously review and accept it. With utmost sincerity, the Jiading County Education Association bows.

Inspect the management status of people's education centers in various counties, and conduct random checks on the management status of people's schools. 5. Inspect the actual management status of joint county, county-run, and private secondary schools in the counties inspected. 6. If the counties inspected have county-run teacher training institutions, thoroughly investigate the implementation of their teaching and training.

Titled "Education and Prosperous Shanghai"

Shanghai Branch of the Education Society

Discussing Fundamental Issues of Education

Holding the Eighth Members' Meeting

The Shanghai Branch of the Chinese Education Society held its eighth members' meeting at the Ninth Floor of the YMCA in the Eight Immortals Bridge the other day, and discussed several fundamental issues of education. The details are as follows:

Members' Meeting: Attendees included Shao Shuangqiu, Shu Xincheng, Zeng Zuozhong, Huang Juemin, Zheng Xigu, Ouyuan Huai, Zha Liangzhao, Chen Xuanshan, Zhang Zhonghuan, Chen Kemei, Sun Kangzeng, Gao Zhisheng, etc. The following motions were discussed: (1) Re-electing the executive officers, it was decided to elect them by mail. (2) Collecting membership dues, it was decided to collect one yuan from each person first. (3) Deciding on the convener of the next meeting, it was decided that the four gentlemen Zha Liangzhao, Sun Kangzeng, Guo Yicen, and Chen Heqin would convene the meeting, scheduled to be held on the afternoon of March 30th. The rest is omitted.

Discussing Issues: The discussion then turned to "Several Fundamental Issues in Education." (A) Outline of the Issues: Regarding the social purpose of education, (1) whether to follow the established educational goals to cultivate good citizens under the political and economic system of the current society, (2) whether to rely on education to create a pre-planned new social system, overturn the old system, and use schools to plant a new social foundation, (3) whether to provide a rich environment to fully develop each child, allow them to freely choose their needs, and be able to recreate their society. (B) Regarding national (state) and world (international) goals, (1) whether to educate all children in the country to prioritize the needs of the country and to give less weight to their own conscience, or vice versa, (2) whether to adopt the same attitude towards obedience to the law, (3) when teaching national history, should children be given a purely objective and accurate view, or should the accuracy of historical facts be sacrificed to cultivate in children a certain ideal or the psychology of worshiping national heroes.

Members' Opinions: (1) Chen Kemei's opinion is divided into (1) an analysis of this issue, (2) which can be summarized into the following two issues, namely the attitude of education and the power of education. (2) Zheng Xiyu's opinion is divided into (1) the several directions of education proposed by this issue do not conflict absolutely, (2) the national education policy and the free development of children complement each other, (3) transforming society based on the needs of current facts. (3) Ou Yuanhuai's opinion is divided into (1) this is a problem of the individual and the environment, (2) transforming the individual to adapt to the environment, or changing the environment to adapt to the individual, or both parties change to establish a suitable relationship, (3) educators should be pioneers and strive for social transformation, and should not follow the crowd. (4) Shao Shuangqiu's opinion is divided into (1) educators should teach children to adapt to the environment, (2) this issue is a question of which of the three paths of capitalism, communism, and fascism to follow. (5) Shu Xincheng's opinion is divided into (1) the purpose of education must be transferred according to politics, and the specific approach should be determined by national policy, so education is a tool, (2) education is political and also supra-political, (3) the purpose of education is to create a cooperative society and a self-reliant individual, (4) education funding should be borne by the state. (6) Chen Qingshi's opinion is that in reality, this issue is two attitudes, that is, whether to regard education as a tool or as an end. (7) Zha Liangzhao's opinion is divided into (1) each person's attitude cannot be forced to be the same, (2) the close relationship between political education, (3) thinking of the following two questions based on personal experience, one is whether the affairs we are doing in the school now are education, and the other is whether the current schools can be regarded as educational institutions. The members discussed the above issues in detail for four hours before finishing.

Sun Yat-sen Cultural and Educational Center

Supplementary Notes on the Anniversary Speech of the Establishment

The other day, the Sun Yat-sen Cultural and Educational Center held its first anniversary celebration. The chairman of the board, Sun Zhesheng, was in Beijing on official business and specially entrusted Ye Gongchuo to represent him as chairman. The grand occasion was reported in various newspapers. We have learned that the speeches of the directors at that time had slight discrepancies, so we are supplementing the notes as follows:

Director Li Shizeng: Briefly stated that the work of this center is based on the teachings of the Premier, and there are many issues, so many that one does not know where to start. Today, I will only extract two words from Sun Yat-sen's ideology, or rather the ideology of this center, which is "mutual assistance." The meaning of mutual assistance is very common. In theory, it is mutual assistance versus competition; in ideology, it is mutual assistance versus struggle. Whether to adopt competition or struggle is a question not only for those outside the party, but also for many comrades within the party. The rampant behavior of the Communist Party in recent years is also due to a misunderstanding of this meaning. The Premier mentioned it very concisely in his teachings, briefly stating that "the state and society are bodies of mutual assistance..." The entire nation and the entire party, whether in the theory or ideology of mutual assistance, should apply it culturally or educationally. Last year, this center mainly focused its scholarships on biology, and this year it will mainly focus on education, which is in line with this meaning.

Director Kong Yongzhi: Briefly stated that the Premier struggled for forty years, completely embracing the ideology of sacrifice and saving the world. His spirit can be left as a lasting memorial for future generations, namely this sacrifice for the people and not for individuals, and the aspiration to save China and save the world. The most important thing for revolutionaries is to talk less and do more, how to implement the ideology, how to instill it into the masses, and how to spread it to the world. To achieve this goal, everyone must work hard. Those who gather here today are all loyal believers of the Premier. The first thing is to learn the Premier's spirit of sacrifice and the ideology of saving the world, and be able to first follow and believe in one's own scope, and then propagate and promote it, starting from China to achieve the realization of a world for all and the great harmony of the world. Only by shouldering this mission can we be worthy of being loyal believers of the Premier. I am willing to encourage this with my dear comrades.

Director Cai Yuanpei: Briefly stated that the Sun Yat-sen Cultural and Educational Center is to inherit the Premier's legacy and carry it forward. The Premier's forty years of revolution focused on politics. Looking at his teachings, politics is also the most prominent. Politics cannot be carried out alone and must be promoted by culture. The last chapter of nationalism talks about how Chinese culture is higher than European culture. The chapters on knowing is easy but doing is difficult and industrial construction have many citations, such as how China was the first to have the compass, printing, and gunpowder. Mr. Zhesheng's initiation of the Cultural and Educational Center is also in view of the fact that various levels of government have taken on the matters that need to be done in politics. For the sake of division of labor, there must be an organization to do cultural work. Culture includes too much, so we should prioritize what is urgent. The chairman just reported that the undertakings that have been carried out in recent years are already quite numerous, and it is good if they can be continued for a long time. Such as land survey, detailed research to find solutions, is not only a Chinese problem, but also a major problem in the world. For education, go to various places for inspection, there are things that should be improved, things that should be promoted, and things that need to be experimented with. Proposing solutions will definitely contribute a lot to the country. Scholarships and financial aid help poor and hardworking scholars, and it would be very good if they could create a few inventors. As for the library, since the Eastern Library was looted, it has not been able to recover. This center's ability to expand and establish a large library is also what the times need. The current affairs compilation and periodical index are valuable because they are continuous. Therefore, it is hoped that those who have already started will continue to work hard and that they will be very impressive in the long run. But everything is never satisfied, and if this center has the opportunity to promote other things, my personal opinion is that we must pay attention to cultural arts, especially art history. The scope of culture is very broad, and China can boast of three major inventions, but its progress is not as good as others. What people compliment us on are (1) philosophy, (2) literature, (3) art. China's culture does not yet have a complete history. Some people are now engaged in the history of philosophy and the history of literature, and it is hoped that they will succeed, but very few people are working on art history, because the materials on display are difficult for individuals to handle, so we must rely on the power of the public. I hope that this center will continue the undertakings that have already been started, and devote its remaining energy to this work.

Pharmacist with a Doctorate from Germany

Mr. Yu Wenfan Returns Home Yesterday

Yu Wenfan from Jiangdu is 32 years old. He previously studied at the Beijing Industrial College. In the 14th year of the Republic (1925), he went to Germany for further studies at his own expense and was admitted to the Chemistry Department of the University of Berlin. In the 20th year of the Republic (1931), he passed the Bachelor of Chemistry examination. Under the guidance of Professor Maurice, the Dean of the School of Pharmacy at the University of Berlin, he researched his doctoral thesis. He completed his thesis in the summer of the 22nd year of the Republic (1933) and passed the doctoral examination in the winter, graduating with honors and obtaining a doctorate. He returned home last month aboard the German ship "Fulda" and arrived in Shanghai yesterday. It is said that after returning to China, Mr. Yu will dedicate his knowledge to China's medical field.

Special Feature

Report on Vocational Education from the Ministry of Education's Investigation in Europe (15)

Navigation Education: Twenty years ago, very little attention was paid to navigation education in Italy, as it was believed that the shipping industry did not require an educational foundation. Later, as the government gradually realized the importance of the shipping industry to the nation's lifeline, it vigorously promoted it. There are now 17 schools and one higher education institution. The schools are divided into classes for mechanics, drivers, and shipbuilding. The higher education institution has departments for driving skills, economics, and other subjects.

The budget is 5,930,000 Italian lire, with 4,150,000 subsidized by the government and 1,780,000 from donations.

Commercial Education: Italian commercial schools are now divided into two types: national commercial schools and national commercial colleges. This is the result of the reorganization of secondary education through the decrees of 1924 and 1925. National commercial schools have a two-year program, and only junior high school students or students from preliminary commercial preparatory classes can be admitted.

National commercial colleges have a five-year program, and only graduates of three years of junior high school can be admitted. Private commercial schools recognized by the government can receive annual subsidies.

(2) School Visit Records

Rome National Institute of Arts and Crafts: This school is one of the royal vocational schools, divided into four departments: mechanics, electrical engineering, architecture, and radio. The program is five years. Common courses include Italian language, religion, history, geography, geometry, physics, natural science, mechanics, economics, and foreign languages. Other departmental courses include: mechanics and electrical engineering department: mechanical drawing, thermodynamics, hydraulics, electrical engineering, electrical practice, steam engines and machinery, materials science, mechanics; architecture department: geometric drawing, architectural drawing, architecture, building materials, materials testing laboratory, architectural model room; radio department: circuit diagrams, thermodynamics, electrical engineering, radio science, radio communication, telephone and telegraph, radio regulations, radio practice. The weekly workload is 48 hours, with 24 hours of theory and 24 hours of practice.

Apprentice Schools: The program is three years, focusing on training machine repairers, metalworkers, and machinists. The weekly workload is also 48 hours, with 18 hours of theory and 30 hours of practice.

Attached Night School: Trains short-term graduates as car drivers, telegraph operators, machine repairers, etc. There are about 400 students, with a weekly workload of 10 to 12 hours.

Equipment: 1. Electrical practice workshop, 2. Aircraft machine experiment laboratory, 3. Carpentry workshop, 4. Foundry workshop, 5. Metal workshop, 6. Radio machine manufacturing room, 7. Radio experiment laboratory, 8. Radio reporting practice room. The school's equipment, especially for aircraft machines and radio machinery, is particularly complete.

Milan Women's Vocational School: This school is purely a training institution. In addition to vocational courses for women, it also runs kindergarten classes and a five-year primary school. Therefore, the total study time here ranges from ten to eleven years. Vocational training is divided into three departments: (1) home economics, (2) cooking, (3) childcare. Sewing, laundry, baking, and ironing are all practical courses. Cooking courses also emphasize planning, such as the raw materials, functions, and price standards of food, which are explained in detail. Students must record the food preparation methods for reference. Dressmaking is based on paper patterns. Students first draw the size with pencil lines on the paper pattern and then cut the finished product as the initial training. The patterns used in embroidery courses are designed and planned by the students themselves to train their creative abilities.

Genoa Maritime School: Only junior high school graduates can be admitted. The program is four years, divided into three departments: mechanics, drivers, and shipbuilding. Graduates can enter naval schools or senior business colleges.

Florence School of Agriculture and Forestry: Only high school graduates can be admitted. The level is similar to that of a university. It only admits 30 to 50 new students each year, divided into two departments: forestry and agriculture. Most graduates work for government agricultural and forestry enterprises.

The curriculum places great emphasis on mountain development, such as storing water volume, focusing on irrigation, planting forests, and studying the suitability of soil properties on mountains as a preparation for planting various types of wood.

Research on plant pathology, plant pests, and the relationship between wood fiber and the paper and rayon industries.

6. Vocational Education in Austria

Vocational education in Austria is managed by local governments in each province, while the highest administrative body is the central government's Ministry of Commerce and Industry. It is divided into six sections dealing with school inspections, teachers and teacher unions, legal issues, general education consultations, commercial education museums, arts and crafts schools, supplementary schools, women's vocational schools, chemical arts and crafts schools, architecture schools, central textile schools, mechanical schools, electrical schools, etc.

Various Industry Groups and Local Chambers of Commerce: Knowing that the level of knowledge of industrial and commercial service personnel is crucial to business prosperity, they often maintain and promote the progress of various vocational schools. For the sake of business development, the General Association for the Promotion of Industry and Commerce is established in Vienna, the capital of Austria, with branches in various places attached to local chambers of commerce. Vocational schools and the Association for the Promotion of Industry and Commerce often have close cooperation. Schools cultivate service technicians for industry and commerce, while representatives from the industrial and commercial sectors provide guidance on educational policies to the schools. Prominent figures in the industry often give public lectures.

Local vocational schools often have school committees composed of representatives from local industry, commerce, and vocational circles, as well as school principals and teachers, who meet to discuss and seek genuine cooperation between schools and society.

(1) Types of Vocational Schools

Most vocational schools are public, but there are also private ones, mostly women's vocational schools. The Austrian school system has eight years of compulsory primary education, divided into basic schools and senior primary schools, each for four years. After completing eight years of primary school, most students enter schools for agriculture, industry, commerce, or women's home economics. After selection, senior primary school students are divided into groups A and B. Group A students enter secondary schools, while group B students enter vocational schools.

Vocational schools are divided into two levels: higher-level schools, such as senior industrial, agricultural, and commercial schools, and lower-level schools, such as general vocational schools, specialized vocational schools, and women's vocational schools.

General Vocational Schools: These schools focus on training practical knowledge and skills for industrial and commercial service personnel. Their level is equivalent to that of a secondary school. The program is four years. Graduates can enter senior industrial schools or senior commercial schools if their grades are excellent.

Specialized Vocational Schools: Specialized training focuses on teaching the skills of one industry or trade. They can replace apprentice training in factories and shops. The program is three years. However, these schools are not limited to training apprentices. Skilled artisans and craftsmen often become talented through specialized vocational school training.

Foreman Schools are a type of specialized vocational school, specifically training technical management personnel for construction, machinery, electrical, and woodworking factories. The program is four semesters.

Women's Vocational Schools: There are four types of public women's vocational schools: 1. Women's vocational schools, 2. Home economics schools, 3. Sewing schools, 4. Teacher training schools. The admission requirements are that students must have received primary school education and be at least 14 years old. For home economics schools, the age requirement is at least 16 years old. Children of merchants and those with experience are given priority in admission, but all must pass an examination to be admitted. (2) Overview of Vocational Schools

Vienna, as the capital of Austria, is the center of the country's essence and a hub of industry and commerce. Therefore, vocational education is quite developed, with more schools and a wider range of disciplines. The length of study varies greatly, depending on the needs of the discipline. For example, the curriculum for general vocational schools is set at four years, but it can be shortened to two or three years due to the simplicity of the discipline or extended to five years due to the complexity of the discipline. The following schools are well-known vocational schools in Vienna:
