Social Circles

On the Necessary Understanding of International Wireless Stations (Part 1)

— Chen Tianzuo

For more than fifty years, China's international telecommunications business has been operated by foreign submarine cable companies, resulting in the loss of sovereignty and the outflow of profits, with annual losses exceeding mere tens of thousands! In recent years, with the rise of the wireless business, the National Government of China, in order to safeguard sovereignty and recover losses, established the International Wireless Station. The establishment process and internal situation have been recorded in the fourth issue of this journal and need not be repeated. However, because China's international telecommunications have long been manipulated and controlled by foreigners, the general merchants and people have become accustomed to sending telegrams through submarine cables and lack a deep understanding of the newly emerging state-run International Wireless Station. This is of great importance to the future of the country. Therefore, this article is written to inform the people of the country.

An independent and autonomous country must maintain the integrity of its telecommunications sovereignty. This is because telecommunications are to the country what the blood vessels are to the human body, closely related and not subject to erosion. International telecommunications, as the ears and eyes of the country, are even more important to a country's economy, diplomacy, and military affairs and must be fought for. Our International Wireless Station was born under this situation, hoping to make up for the shortcomings and complete the mission of recovering submarine cable rights.

Now, please allow me to describe the relationship between the International Wireless Station and China's economy, diplomacy, and military affairs so that the concept of benefits and harms will be deeply imprinted in the minds of the people, who will not forget the importance of the station at all times and will strive to assist its development.

First, let us talk about the economy.

When a country's international telecommunications are controlled by others, the power to control the telegraph fee is entirely in the hands of others, which goes without saying. The telegraph fees earned by various submarine cable companies in China are mostly taken by the company, with China only sharing a small portion of the remaining profits. This loss is about 8 million yuan per year, totaling nearly 400 million yuan over more than fifty years. This is only the tangible loss. The loss from using this telecommunications equipment to manipulate China's international market is hundreds or thousands of times greater. The International Wireless Station has always negotiated the allocation of telegraph fees with various countries in the spirit of mutual benefit and equality, and the distribution is very fair. Now, a comparison of the allocation of telegraph fees for submarine cable and wireless telegraphs is listed below for reference:

Comparative Table of International Telegraph Fee Allocation

Looking at the table above, the difference in the telegraph fees that China should receive between wireless and submarine cables is significant. Now that the International Wireless Station has been established, most countries have abandoned the former and chosen the latter when sending international telegrams. This annual loss of several million yuan can be slightly stopped from now on. This is the relationship between the International Wireless Station and China's national economy.

New Characters in the Newly Compiled Code

The Ministry of Communications published a new edition of the Clear-Secret Code in August of last year, with 138 new characters added, which has been convenient for all sectors since its publication. Now, according to the request of various telegraph bureaus, five more characters are needed, and the Ministry of Communications has ordered all telegraph stations to add them. The codes for the added characters are listed below.

虬 5874 壋 8250 裯 8874 砟 8875 9351

Voice of the Telegraph World

Official Military Telegrams

— Lü Bing

Urgent as Saving a Fire

In the previous issue of this journal, the reporter compared the transmission of telegrams with the driving of vehicles on the road, finding that the situations were very similar. The official military urgent telegram is like a fire engine. According to the International Telegraph Regulations, official telegrams are classified as first-class. Official telegrams marked as urgent (in fact, there is no such thing as urgent in official telegrams, but Chinese official telegrams always have these words before the text) must be sent in advance.

Official military urgent telegrams have a significant direct impact on politics or military affairs, and indirectly affect domestic security and the lives of the people. The advance sending of telegrams can quell chaos in its infancy and ensure the smooth command. Therefore, urgency is necessary, and the passage of a fire engine is regarded as a matter of life and property, and cannot be delayed. It is said that the situation is the same and the principle is the same. However, during the era of warlord rule, it was selfishly believed that telegrams could be made faster (in fact, telegrams are sent according to regulations and there is no delay). Therefore, regardless of whether the nature was important or whether the telegram was related to public affairs, the word "urgent" was added before the telegram. Later, it progressed rapidly, accumulating and using words such as "extremely urgent," "flying extremely urgent," "one hundred thousand or even one million extremely urgent." As a result, all telegrams were flying and no telegram was not urgent. If we compare this to a fire engine, it is as if fire engines are coming and going on the main roads, charging and ramming, and ordinary vehicles have the suffering of not being able to move. If fire engines are everywhere, the streets will be chaotic. If all official military telegrams are flying extremely urgent, is this a good phenomenon?

Now, let us use the car as an analogy again. Fire engines are only suitable for putting out fires and should not be used to carry passengers. Similarly, official military telegrams should only be related to public affairs and should not involve private matters. Therefore, a telegram that is official in name but private in reality is no different from a fire engine that does not put out fires but carries passengers privately. Now, the political and military authorities are different from before. Once the Ministry of Communications implements measures to crack down on official military private telegrams, they will be able to consider the situation and understand the principles, so that the telegraph lines can be cleared up.

Telephone Line Components

— Wang Qikun

The components of telephone lines, whether for urban or long-distance use, differ in quality, using either iron or copper wire, and in quantity, using either single or double wires.

Iron wire is inexpensive and sturdy, making it more economical; however, its electrical resistance is higher and it has a skin effect, making it unsuitable for voice currents. Copper wire is the opposite, so except in special circumstances, copper wire is typically used for telephone lines. In long-distance telephony, due to the long distances involved, the conductivity of voice current is particularly important, so the use of copper wire is also the principle.

If telephones use a single wire with the earth as a return path, the initial costs can be reduced by almost half. However, earth communication often produces earth currents, which can affect the call. Furthermore, electric trams, power lines, electric lights, etc., often have one end of their return circuits connected to the earth, and the leakage current can infiltrate telephone lines and disrupt calls. Therefore, double-wire systems are suitable for ordinary urban telephone lines, and single-wire systems are especially unsuitable for long-distance telephones that pass through several cities.

The use of double wires for long-distance telephones has the following additional benefits: (1) Double current operation (simultaneous telephone and telegraph communication) can be adopted, which could facilitate combined telegraph transmission and reception, or allow the telephone line to be used as an auxiliary line. The so-called use as an auxiliary line means that two operators can switch to telegraphy when communicating, to increase the efficiency of the telephone line. (2) It can be converted into a phantom circuit, where two pairs of wires can be used as three pairs, four pairs of wires can be used as six pairs—even used as seven pairs of telephone lines and one pair of telegraph lines; with wider paths, transmission can be accelerated. (3) Carrier systems can be used to make one pair of wires serve as four to sixteen pairs, increasing the utilization of the telephone line.

Looking at the long-distance telephone lines in various parts of the country, those used for military purposes mostly use single-wire iron wire, while those operated by provinces or businesses use double-wire copper wire, but many also use single-wire iron wire. Those operated by the Ministry of Communications—such as Beijing-Shanghai, Shanghai-Hangzhou, Beijing-Tianjin, Qingdao-Jinan—are all double-wire copper wire, and Beijing-Shanghai even adopts double current operation and phantom circuits, becoming a good friend of wired and wireless telegraphy.

Based on the components of long-distance telephone lines in various locations, it is not difficult to infer their service performance. Furthermore, the electrical communication business must meet the following conditions in order to fully demonstrate its effectiveness: (1) speed, (2) accuracy, (3) stability and reliability, (4) low cost, (5) simple procedures, (6) ability to supply large quantities of needs, and (7) maintaining secrecy. Among the electrical communication businesses, only well-equipped long-distance telephones can fully meet these seven conditions.

Installation of Wired Telegraph Lines in the Past Year (Middle)

— Qian Jiaguang

Expanded Line Routes

(1) Overview: Existing lines should be repaired, and transportation development should be expanded. Given the vastness and abundance of our country, communication equipment should not be restricted for long. Therefore, the Ministry of Communications is making every effort to repair trunk and branch lines, and at the same time, considering the people, expanding the lines as needed, and developing the communication scope with construction. Generally, the lines added in the 22nd year can be divided into two categories for explanation.

(A) Pertaining to the Bandit Suppression Area—Localities that have become bandit areas have had previous construction completely destroyed. Central troops are constantly advancing to suppress bandits and recover various places, and communication should be restored urgently so that people can rest and recuperate, news can be mutually transmitted, and troop movements can be facilitated.

(B) Pertaining to Business Needs! Inland cities are developing commerce, but telegraph offices have not yet been established. Round-trip telegrams to major trading ports require traveling thousands of miles to send them to nearby offices for transmission, or having nearby offices deliver them by special messengers. This is both inconvenient and time-consuming. Alternatively, the original lines were not sufficient to handle the busy telegram traffic. To meet the needs of the people, it is necessary to expand the lines or add to existing lines.

(2) Statistics: According to the above situation, the expansion of the lines should be divided into two categories: "newly installed lines" and "added wires". The so-called "added wires" means adding additional wires to existing roads to increase efficiency in actual communication. Combining the above two expansions, a total of 3,197 kilometers were completed in the past year. There is also a newly installed underwater line from Datong in Anhui Province to Heyuezhou, with a length of 2,000 feet. The details can be seen below.

(A) Newly Installed Lines—Total length is 2,104 kilometers: Qishui to Yingshan 78 kilometers; Huang'an to Hekouzhen 25 kilometers; Tianjin to Xianshuigu 33 kilometers; Xianshuigu to Gegu 12 kilometers; Daye County seat to Xialu 14 kilometers; Tianjin to Liangwangzhuang 52 kilometers; Jiapu to Dongtang 10 kilometers; Dushan to Liusaitang 104 kilometers; Xing'an to Guanyang 115 kilometers; Tianjin to Dagu 142 kilometers; Fancheng to Zaoyang 86 kilometers; Daokou to Daming 124 kilometers; Yancheng to Guanjia Guan 60 kilometers; Fuzhou to Zhenbian 63 kilometers; Luoyang to Meng County 73 kilometers; Wuxue to Huangmei 69 kilometers; Jianggan to Fuyang 34 kilometers; Pingyuan to Xunwu 121 kilometers; Xiajiang to Jibing 69 kilometers; Xiali River to Jixian 12 kilometers; Longqu to Suichang 69 kilometers; Guangzhou to Shangcheng 55 kilometers; Yongfeng to Anle 58 kilometers; Anle to Chongren 81 kilometers; Shuikou to Gutian 69 kilometers; Fuzhou to Chongren 52 kilometers; Fuzhou to Yihuang 75 kilometers; Niukou to Wushan 81 kilometers; Fuzhou to Jinxi 58 kilometers; Pucheng via Longquan to Qingyuan 210 kilometers.

(B) Added Wires—Total length is 1,093 kilometers: Wuxi to Jiangyin 40 kilometers; Wushan to Kuizhou 69 kilometers; Huzhou to Jiapu 59 kilometers; Hejigang to Daye 71 kilometers; Caidian to Shashi 276 kilometers; Beiping to Yutian 119 kilometers; Beiping to Tangshan 35 kilometers; Beiping to Zhangjiakou 243 kilometers; Hangzhou to Chang'an 52 kilometers; Dezhou to Yancheng 89 kilometers.

Discussing the Convenience of Sending Telegrams in Shanghai

— Ji Qing

Bureau Stations and Receiving/Dispatching Branches

Total 19 Locations

Nowadays, sending a telegram is truly very convenient. Because telegraph bureaus or wireless stations in various locations, in addition to receiving and dispatching telegrams at their own bureau stations, have also added receiving/dispatching branches or receiving stations in busy and convenient locations, in order to facilitate telegram sending for people who are further away. Then, people who send telegrams do not necessarily have to go to the telegraph bureau or wireless station; they can send telegrams at the nearby receiving/dispatching branch or receiving station, and they can also quickly reach all parts of the world or the country.

We who live in Shanghai feel that sending telegrams is even more convenient than elsewhere. Because the international radio stations, telegraph bureaus, wireless stations, the receiving/dispatching branches of various bureau stations, and the various receiving stations attached to the Shanghai Bank and its branches, as well as the various submarine line receiving/dispatching stations, large and small, number nearly twenty. They are scattered everywhere, like stars in the sky, so that there is a bureau every five steps, a station across the street, a receiving/dispatching branch around the corner, and a receiving station across the street. Therefore, sending telegrams is truly very convenient!

Now, in order to let everyone know the locations of the various bureau stations, receiving/dispatching branches, and receiving stations, I will list them one by one (see above in this publication) so that everyone can check them at any time.

All telegraph bureaus, wireless stations, receiving/dispatching branches, and receiving stations are under the jurisdiction of the Ministry of Communications. All staff members have strict orders from the ministry to operate commercially, implement measures for the public, and act politely. If they put on airs of being officials, are perfunctory in their work, or are impolite to senders and receivers, then please report them to the supervisors without hesitation, so that they will be strictly investigated and dealt with, and efforts will be made to improve.

Recent Developments in Overseas Wireless Radio

— Fang

Anglo-French Aviation Shortwave Communication

For the sake of maintaining the safety of civil aviation, the aviation departments of the United Kingdom and France have specifically installed ultra-shortwave radio transceivers between the Lympne and Angleville aviation stations on both sides of the English Channel for liaison communication. The distance between the two stations is approximately 35 miles. The wavelength used is approximately seven inches. The results of the bilateral tests were very satisfactory. This ultra-shortwave communication not only avoids various interferences in the air, but also guarantees the confidentiality and stability of communication. It is reported that this route of communication was officially opened on January 26 of this year. At present, the business is limited to receiving and dispatching telegrams reporting the departure and arrival times of aircraft.

Mackay Company's Newly Established Radio Stations

The new Chicago, New Orleans, and Seattle radio stations established by the American Mackay Radio Telegraph Company opened for communication in December of last year. Together with the original four stations in New York, San Francisco, Los Angeles, and Portland, there are now a total of seven domestic radio stations. The company and Postal Telegraph are both affiliated companies of International Telephone & Telegraph (ITT) Corporation, and the two parties have always adopted a cooperative approach in their business. Therefore, if the customers of Postal Telegraph want to send telegrams to the above-mentioned seven locations, they can all be transmitted by Mackay Company's radio stations. Mackay Company started operating domestic wireless radio business in 1911. At that time, radio stations were established in major cities along the Pacific coast to receive and dispatch commercial reports. It was not until 1914 that marine communication between the United States and the Hawaiian Islands was started. The current international wireless radio routes can directly reach Denmark, Hungary, Austria, the Vatican, Spain, Argentina, Colombia, Peru, Cuba, Hawaii, the Philippines, and China.

The World of Telecommunications

— Zhen

Wireless Telegraph Communication between Spain and the United States

Wireless communication between Spain and the United States was inaugurated by the Mackay Company on November 18 of last year. (News from New York International Telephone and Telegraph Company)

Establishment of Sweden's Largest Radio Broadcasting Station

The Swedish Telegraph Bureau requested the government to allocate 1.4 million Krona (1 Krona equals US$0.267) from the construction fund for the reconstruction of the Motala broadcasting station. The existing power of the station is 30 kilowatts, which can be increased to 150 kilowatts in the future, making it the largest radio station in Sweden. (London Electrical Review)

Hungary's Tallest Antenna Radio Station

The new 120-kilowatt radio station in Budapest has already been opened. Its cigar-shaped radio mast reaches a height of 314 meters, making it the tallest antenna in the world. All components are dual (even crystal oscillators) for emergency needs. The lowest level of the station has four 120-kilowatt gates for propulsion. There is also a special electric button that can cut off the entire power supply in one second in an emergency. (London Electrical Review)

Installation of Swiss Telephone Trunk Lines

The Swiss government has recently been engaged in rebuilding telephone trunk lines in the Valais region that have been stalled for many years. This line runs along the banks of Lake Geneva, across the Rhone plain, to Brig, for a total length of approximately 97 miles. It will be connected to the new Lotschberg Tunnel's telephone submarine lines, and then connected to the Italian telephone lines at Iselle via the Italian key, so that the underground cable between Geneva and Milan can be completed for telephone calls. (London Electrical Review)

Connection of North-South Telephone Lines in the Federated Malay States

The direct telephone line between the British Federated Malay States and Singapore and the northern border of Malaya will be established on November 1. At that time, the existing federal trunk lines will be extended to Kedah and Perlis, which are not part of the Federated Malay States in the northern border of Malaya, so that telephone calls will be possible between the northern and southern parts of the peninsula. (Report from the US Commercial Attaché in Singapore)

Progress of Automatic Telephones in Germany

According to the Post Office, there are currently only eleven automatic telephone exchanges installed in Berlin. This new type of telephone started construction in 1926 and will be completed in 1935. It is planned that there will be eighty exchanges in the city of Berlin, which currently has approximately 260,000 telephone subscribers. (Report from the US Commercial Attaché in Berlin)

Achievements of Japanese Wire Manufacturers

The Japanese Sumitomo Electric Wire & Cable Co. was ordered by the Ministry of Communications to establish a submarine cable manufacturing plant in Shirinashi, southwest of Osaka (where 10,000-ton vessels can be docked) in February of the year before last. The plant site covers a total of 3,600 tsubo (approximately three acres), of which 1,400 tsubo (approximately one acre) are for factory offices and ancillary buildings. Its machinery can manufacture various insulated submarine cables. This is the only factory in Japan that manufactures submarine cables, and Japan is now able to manufacture these submarine cables independently without having to rely on foreigners. The first products of the factory were submarine cables for the Taiwan local government to connect seven nautical miles, and later, several Tokyo Bay telephone submarine cables and a 57-nautical-mile telephone submarine cable in the Korean Strait were installed for the Japanese government. Currently, it is undertaking the manufacture of various types of custom submarine cables, with a total length of approximately several hundred nautical miles. (Far Eastern Review)

Bi-Monthly News

— A Member of the Society

Postal Remittance Bureau's Fee Collection Methods for Telegraphic Transfers

The Ministry of Communications, in order to facilitate communication for the public and save expenses, previously instructed the relevant postal and telegraph authorities to consult on cooperative measures. In addition to the joint establishment of postal and telegraph bureaus and the exemption of postage for postal transfers of telegrams, which have been recorded in the previous issue of this publication, there is also a method for collecting fees for telegraphic transfers issued by postal remittance bureaus, which has also been agreed upon and will be implemented from March 15. The main points of the method are extracted and recorded below:

1. For telegraphic transfers issued by the Postal Savings Remittance General Branch and post offices concurrently handling savings and remittance business, regardless of whether the telegram text is in Chinese or foreign languages, clear or coded, a flat fee of six jiao (silver yuan) will be charged for each telegram within 20 characters. For each character exceeding the limit, an additional five fen (silver yuan) will be charged.

2. If these telegraphic transfers need to be sent as urgent telegrams, the above-mentioned prices should be doubled. If checking is required, half the fee should be added.

3. These telegraphic transfers should be marked with "MDT" before the name, address, and place name of the recipient, and counted as one character for billing purposes.

The above-mentioned fee collection method for telegraphic transfers is only applicable to those issued by postal remittance bureaus. Telegraphic transfers issued by other banks will still be charged at ordinary prices. It is reported that the Ministry of Communications has given a special discount for telegraphic transfers issued by postal remittance bureaus because, firstly, from March 15, the postage for postal transfers of telegrams will be exempted. Secondly, the various remittances received by postal remittance bureaus are mostly less than 100 yuan. In order to facilitate the public, the fees for telegraphic transfers have been reduced, so that the general public can quickly remit funds in urgent need by spending a few jiao on telegram fees.

Furthermore, the total amount exchanged at the Shanghai Clearing House on the 15th was 9,510,059.22 yuan, including 3,423,513.95 yuan in silver dollars and 6,086,545.27 yuan in exchange transfers of silver dollars.

Continued Fall in Guangjiao, Extension of Copper Coin Supply

Yesterday, there was no change in Jiangnan small silver coins, remaining the same as the previous day at 810 yuan. Trading volume was 5,000 jiao in the morning and 4,000 jiao in the afternoon. Guangdong small silver coins fell by slightly over two yuan, entering the 60 yuan range. The morning price was 760.6 yuan, and the afternoon price dropped to only 759 yuan. Trading volume was 45,000 jiao in the morning and 70,000 jiao in the afternoon. Copper coins were at 320,500 cash, an increase of 1,500 cash compared to the previous day. 31,127 strings were traded, with a total value of 9,400 yuan in silver.

Securities

Bond Market Shows Signs of Activity as Settlement Date Approaches

—Market Slightly Firmer, Showing Signs of Rising—

Yesterday, the Shanghai Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange saw a slightly stronger market. Some people believed that the Japanese attitude towards Chahar seemed unstable again, and that the market might ease. The insensitivity of market prices was also due to short sellers slightly rolling over their positions. Although the number was not large, the trend relied on firmness. It is evident that the current situation still places importance on the different supply and demand of chips. At the opening in the morning, scattered short sellers and No. 75 short sellers rolled over their positions, but with limitations, unwilling to ease market prices, so their bidding was very firm, with a slight upward trend of about one or two jiao. From the second session to the close, although the fluctuations were small, the trend was extremely stable and slightly bullish. Compared to before, it seemed to be slightly more active. Measuring its shape, its volatility should gradually show signs of activity, as the settlement date gradually approaches. As a result, market prices uniformly returned by one to four jiao. The total transaction volume was 4,933,000 yuan, including 3,000 yuan in spot goods and 4,930,000 yuan in futures. Mixed Performance in New York Stock Market

According to a report from the New Feng Foreign Firm, the New York stock market on the 14th showed mixed results, slightly higher overall. Railroad freight transportation continued to increase, the St. Lawrence Seaway Treaty failed to pass in the Senate, and positive commercial news outweighed negative news. However, steel production did not expand due to the automobile industry strike. The New York State government threatened to restrict public utility companies, leading bulls to close positions slightly. The small exchange market was firm, with bond prices reaching new highs, especially for industrial companies, railroads, and speculative public utility companies. High-grade bonds and U.S. government bonds were also firm, while foreign government bonds were mixed. The total daily trading volume was 1.36 million shares. The wheat market was stable with slightly increased trading and better news. The harvest was light, and news from the Southwest favored bulls. Cotton futures trading was dull, while spot trading was firm due to the proposal to reduce factory work to 30 hours per week. However, prices were firm and stable. Opposition was expected in Congress to preferential cotton loans to the Soviet Union. According to various reports, American farmers were planting cotton in Mexico because the government's restrictions could not reach abroad. U.S. cotton consumption in February totaled 477,900 bales. Spun Yarn

Local Cotton Mills to Reduce Working Hours Starting June 1st

—Yarn Market Continues to Rise in the Morning, Slightly Retreats in the Afternoon—

The yarn market saw a strong upward trend in the morning due to the successful conclusion of the factory meeting the previous day, which resulted in a uniform reduction of working hours starting June 1st. This caused scattered short sellers to panic and rush to buy in to cover their positions, further fueling the upward trend. However, rumors circulated in the market in the afternoon that the British Jardine Matheson factory had released 3-4,000 pieces of 20-count Five Blessings brand yarn, but the price and buyers had not yet been announced, slightly impacting and weakening the market.

Standard Yarn Continues to Rise

The standard yarn market opened in the forenoon, advancing on the previous day's firmness, with short covering activities, each month rising between 0.27 and 1.12 yuan. The market sentiment turned weaker again in the afternoon, with profit-takers closing positions. Each month rose by 0.34 yuan. The total trading volume for the day was 66,400 bales. Upon investigation, Hengda sold 1,400 bales, Dafu 1,050 bales, Dafeng 2,950 bales, Taixing 1,200 bales, Shenchang 1,700 bales, Dachangcheng 1,700 bales, Yuanfeng 2,050 bales, Changfeng 850 bales, and Yichang 950 bales. Grains

Dullness in the Flour Futures Market

—Not Many Sellers, Outcome Still Flat—

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market, the market for each month presented a state of initial stability followed by weakness. Quotations for foreign wheat were around 48 points below for Chicago and 0.20 yuan below for Canadian wheat. At the opening, because the market had more upward momentum, the opening prices for each month were slightly better by 0.005-0.01 yuan compared to the previous day. Later, because actual sales were inactive and small factories only made a few accommodation sales, the market turned flat again. In the afternoon opening, the market in each month generally hovered, but because sellers were not smooth, the outcome slightly rebounded. However, transactions in each session were extremely quiet. In recent markets, vitality has been lacking, the main reason being the dryness of the economy in various regions and lack of purchasing power, and artificial manipulations are ineffective. As a result, the current month was slightly lower by 0.025 yuan, April was slightly better by 0.05 yuan, May and June were unchanged, and July and August were better by 0.05 yuan.

Lacking Activity in Forward Wheat Trading

Yesterday, the market for forward wheat remained extremely quiet. Although foreign wheat quotations were still slightly lower by 48 points to 0.20 yuan, the standard situation ultimately lacked significant changes. The market for the current month was already softened due to the inclusion of foreign wheat. In the context of sluggish flour sales, although squeezing shorts was successful, there was no real benefit. Moreover, those with foreign wheat could take the opportunity to sell it off. Forward contracts lacked activity in both buying and selling because the prospect of domestic wheat harvests was uncertain. The result was that the current month was slightly lower by 0.02 yuan, and all others were unchanged. Spot wheat was not traded because factory demand had stopped.

Sales of Late Rice Continue, Up 0.05 Yuan

—All Heavy Geng Stays the Same—

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, there were over 40 traders and over 6,000 shih of supplies. The market initially remained sluggish, but fortunately, visiting merchants gradually arrived, tightening the situation. As a result, the current flat situation was maintained. The market prices for commonly traded Su Tong, Nanhang, and other Geng rice showed no change. However, the buying interest from out-of-town traders began with the Beiyang traders from Tianjin, Yantai, etc., and then the Nanyang and Xiamen traders followed suit, making the market seem to rise. However, the Nanyang traders suddenly stopped, only purchasing 3-400 bags, thus affecting the market tone. Sellers were forced to lower prices slightly. After hovering like this for about half an hour, fortunately, the Beiyang traders continued to purchase, making it turn slightly better. By the close, the statistics showed that the Beiyang and Nanyang traders purchased a total of two shiploads of thick Geng rice, and 3,300-3,400 bags of Qingjiao, Songsi, Xilian, and Fengjing Nanhang late rice, thus allowing the late rice market price to continue to rise by 0.05 yuan. Du Yangjiansales were still acceptable and remained stable. The sales of Yinbian Yuandian were slightly better, but the market did not show strength.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, there were 47-48 traders of various goods from Hexia, and the sales of various goods in the market were slightly active. The market for Bai Geng was flat in the morning and settled in the afternoon. The price of early thin rice was reduced by several points. Yang Du, Bu Ke, Jian Bian, and Yin Yuan had no significant changes.

Xiang Rice Sells Well, Continues to Rise

—Foreign Rice Price Reductions Sought to Sell—

Yesterday, the situation in the Xiang rice market was excellent. Because production prices have been rising recently, the source has been gradually reduced. The Xiang provincial authorities have begun to collect and store 500,000 bags of rough rice in warehouses, and the cost of Xiang province rough rice will gradually increase. Traders in the local market immediately shouted for a price increase of 0.2 yuan, but the inventory in the market was still sufficient, and there were also goods arriving from other provinces, so the market price failed to rise fully. As a result, it continued to rise by 0.12-0.13 yuan and 0.06-0.07 yuan respectively. Other mechanically processed rough rice followed suit. When the market price was first increased in the morning, purchases were still slow, but after the cargo owners slightly lowered the price in the afternoon, traders from Fujian and Zhejiang provinces began to inquire. The appetite of the Fuzhou and Quanzhou traders in Fujian province and the Ningbo and Wenzhou traders in Zhejiang province was greedier. There were also sales to the mainland. Yesterday, the Yongbo traders were greedier, purchasing more than 4,000 bags. The sales interest of other routes was still high, but the rise was too fast, and it was feared that it was not worth transporting. The total number of various mechanically processed rough Xiang rice sold all day was 9,832 bags. One thousand bags of small quantity foreign rice were opened, and 2,500 bags in secret trading. The initial price was 6.7 yuan, then 6.67 yuan, and the lowest price was 6.65 yuan. 1,000 bags were purchased from Ningbo, and the rest were purchased by local street shops. This price was lower than the previous price, because the cargo owners intended to reduce the price in order to sell.

Soybean Factories Trade Intermittently

Yesterday, the soybean market was first soft and then tight. Factories bought and sold in the morning intermittently. The situation still lacked prosperity. Because the buying price was limited and factories only took small quantities of goods, it was difficult to develop for a while. Yesterday, the factory bought about 7,000 bags of Henan Guide Dangshan soybeans, with a market price of 2.5 yuan. An oil workshop in Jiangbei purchased three cars of Linhuaiguan soybeans, with a price of 2.33 yuan. In addition, traders in the local street bought about four or five cars of various round beans for export.

Black Melon Seeds in North-South Goods Sell Weakly, Price Drops

More than a Thousand Bags of Hainan Red Sugar Opened in the Sugar Market

—The Market Is Still Difficult to Be Optimistic About—

The sugar market was sluggish, and the guild barely made any trades. Only Hainan red sugar, due to action by the Yantai traders, opened more than a thousand bags, with a price of 13.3-13.4 yuan, which was 0.1-0.2 yuan lower than before. Although Shantou traders were asking for 13 yuan, there were no buyers. With the current congested inventory, it is still difficult to revitalize the market.

Sales of Cloth, Woolen Goods, and Sichuan Goods are Sluggish

Woolen goods and fabrics are currently selling well, and the number of daily shipments by traders has been increasing, with a stable market trend. However, the Sichuan traders have been slow to act, which is a shame. This is due to tight credit conditions and the upcoming increase in postal parcel taxes. The recent purchase interest of the traders has been slight. Most traders have to receive letters from their superiors before they can make small purchases, lacking the power to independently make purchases. According to experienced traders, there may be a group buying spree in ten days, but most of the light fabrics for spring sales will not be able to make it in time.

Head Sacrifice to Spirits

— Shi Heng

Westerners, even towards their enemies after death, always express a certain respect. Therefore, between people, when encountering irreconcilable feuds, as long as they can defeat their enemies, they no longer haggle over it, and rarely seek revenge on the dead. Moreover, their approach to revenge is only "an eye for an eye," never involving many innocent people.

But in China, things are vastly different: towards enemies, even if they are dead, they cannot be forgiven; Wu Zixu whipping the corpse became a beautiful tale of revenge for all time. Although this is relatively rare, we can easily find similar examples in ordinary books: cutting grass to eradicate roots, killing the enemy's chickens and dogs without leaving any alive. During the Spring and Autumn period, the conflict between the Tu and Zhao families was caused by the loss of an infant less than one year old, and they even wanted to kill all infants of the same age in the city to eliminate future troubles. And usually, after slicing the enemy into a thousand pieces, it is still not enough to vent their anger; they must also sacrifice the bloody heads before the spirits of those who have been dead for many years to feel satisfied.

At the same time, the Chinese attitude towards enemies is also different from that of Westerners. When we read Nordic novels, we often see stories of revenge, but although they hate their enemies, they also respect them. The stronger the opponent, the more they respect them. When the enemy is about to die, they seem to have reached an understanding of friendship with each other, and there will never be any destruction of the enemy's corpse to relieve hatred. Because they respect their enemies, their means of revenge are always honorable and upright, standing in a position of mutual struggle. In China, it is just the opposite. If the enemy is strong, the feud may not be avenged for the time being, and they may even fawn and flatter him, becoming the enemy's running dog; but if the enemy is weak, they will try all kinds of despicable and filthy means to completely eradicate them.

The Chinese attitude of revenge precisely expresses the two special qualities of the Chinese nation, on the one hand, it shows shameful cowardice, and on the other hand, it shows inhumane cruelty. Moreover, from these special qualities of the Chinese nation, which combine cowardice and cruelty, we can better understand why the spirit of "beating a drowning dog" is particularly developed among the Chinese.

Twilight Recital

—

The bleak twilight paints a remote mountain path; a sedan chair hastily passes through an ancient teahouse. Wisps of green smoke float around the steep mountain peaks, and a few crows fly gracefully into the secluded green pine forest. An elderly woodcutter, carrying two bundles of dry firewood, gasps for breath, slowly walking into a dilapidated bamboo gate!

A Stroll in the Confucian Temple

— Zi Ge

There was a period, about two years ago, when I walked in the Confucian Temple almost every day. Of course, "every day" is an average. Actually, sometimes I would go several times a day, and sometimes I wouldn't go for several days.

At that time, I lived next door to the Confucian Temple, separated by an alley called Que Li. During the day, besides doing my own work, I also had to observe the faces of the people who ate and worked with me. At night, my room was always surrounded by young people who were the same age as me or even older, making it suffocating, and there was nowhere to escape. So, I could only sneak into the Confucian Temple for a walk in the morning or evening to get a chance to take a few deep breaths of fresh air.

To get to the Confucian Temple, you could only enter through the side gates on both sides. For the sake of convenience, we always entered from the side gate of the Kong family mansion along Que Li Road. As soon as you entered the gate, you would see many turtle-like objects lying on the ground, with large steles more than ten feet high on their backs. They were all carved from very solid stone, but they couldn't help but make people feel a little pitiful. So, colleagues often pointed at them and joked to others, "How pitiful you are!" At the same time, I also learned that the young people there liked to scold people for being slow by saying, "You are being pressed by a big stele!"

Going up to the right, through a large gate, you could look up and see the Dacheng Hall. Walking down the stone steps, what lies in front of you is the Apricot Platform, said to be where Confucius taught. Right below the stone steps, on the left side, opposite the Apricot Platform, is a long stele inscribed with the five characters "The Former Teacher Planted Cypress," next to which stands a cypress tree, with a section of withered tree trunk framed in glass on the side, said to be the cypress tree planted by Confucius himself, and the living tree is derived from it. The Apricot Platform is a square pavilion with a few small apricot trees in front of it. Only one leaning tree is considered old. I saw them blossom and bear fruit. I picked the apricots to eat, but they didn't taste sweet, so I guess they were newly planted. In the middle of the Apricot Platform, there is something like a bell hanging, said to be the wooden tongue, which sounds good when struck, but one cannot help but suspect that this is an association produced by the sentence "Heaven will take the master as a wooden tongue." Walking straight up, you will reach the front door of the Dacheng Hall. (To be continued)

Cold Water Literature

— Xu Maoyong

When people are excitedly engrossed in something or someone, if someone suddenly makes a penetrating remark to spoil their enthusiasm, in our hometown, this is called "pouring cold water." Pouring a bucket of cold water into a boiling pot can stop the boiling, and even make the heat disappear completely. Enthusiastic young people are not afraid of fierce enemies or repeated setbacks, but they are most afraid of a spoonful of cold water that seems well-intentioned, which makes them suddenly doubt their beliefs and waver, often leading to discouragement. And the intention of pouring cold water is different from that of pouring enlightenment; the latter aims to input wisdom and make people comfortable, which is positive, while the former only aims to negatively destroy people's will, so it can also be said to be a soft knife that kills without bloodshed.

The Chinese people's will is worn down the fastest, young people easily become mature, and the fire of youth burns very briefly, because there is too much cold water in China. Not to mention anything else, just say that most of the ancient and modern literature contains the effect of pouring cold water. This kind of cold water literature has a formula, which is the "Song of Good and Bad" sung by the lame Taoist to Zhen Shiyin in *Dream of the Red Chamber*. Here is one of them:

"The world all knows immortals are good, only fame and fortune they can't forget. Where are the generals and ministers of ancient and modern times? Mounds of graves covered with grass are all that remains."

The simplest example that fits this formula is Li Bai's poem:

"King Goujian of Yue returned after defeating Wu, the warriors returned home in brocade clothes, palace maids like flowers filled the spring palace—now only partridges are seen flying."

This kind of work can be found endlessly in ancient and modern poetry collections, and they are all among the best. In recent times, someone compiled a "Heart-Stirring Melody Collection," which only collected a thin volume of works from ancient and modern times, but if you were to compile a cold water literature collection, it would be so large that it could "reach your height."

Ancient Chinese literature can be roughly divided into two schools: one is the court literature that carries the Confucian way, which is written by successful scholar-officials, talking about positive principles, but it is mostly stale and even unworthy of being called literature. The other school can be said to be pure literature, which mostly comes from the hands of the unsuccessful, influenced by Taoism or Buddhism, because both Taoism and Buddhism advocate transcending the present world, so this school of literature also takes the idea that everything in the present world is empty as its common center.

However, although both Taoism and Buddhism see through the present world, they either advocate returning to nature or advocate rebirth in the Pure Land. On the other hand, they still have their positive beliefs. The lame Taoist's "Song of Good and Bad" ultimately considers immortals to be good and "completion" as the destination, so it has not yet fallen into nihilism and is not entirely cold water literature. As for those who thoroughly deny even immortals and do not believe in the Pure Land, that is truly cold water literature, but there is a contradiction in it. Those who have no faith and cannot be completed are bitter, but this bitterness is not impossible to dispel. The way to dispel it is to curse the present world while still using everything in the present world to anesthetize one's soul, raise a glass to dispel sorrow, and end up confused: hence the saying that it is rare to be confused in life.

Some of today's humor literature is also cold water literature. It considers itself to be a transcendental school, observing the world with a cold eye and mocking everything, not only laughing at those who diligently pursue profit, but also laughing at those who diligently pursue righteousness, not only laughing at what others cry about, but also laughing at what others laugh about. No matter how big or small the matter is, no matter how wise or foolish the person is, they are all doused with cold water, thinking that they have succeeded. This is the attitude of many humorists today. Mr. Lin Yutang advocates humor with the gentle and honest poetry teaching as advice, but the most popular attitude among most of our humorists is, as Pett Ridge said, "It is better to mock the protagonist of a story than to laugh along with him." The difference cannot be measured in miles.

If you were to investigate what the positive beliefs of these humorists who mock everything are, they would probably be confused. The British humor magazine *Punch* once published a humorous story: "Two Englishmen in Paris once passed a store and saw the words 'English Spoken' written on the door. They went in to shop, but saw that the saleswoman did not speak a word of English. So one of them asked in incorrect French, 'Who speaks English?' The saleswoman replied, 'The English-speaking customers do.'"

This is a good example of the confused category in humorous literature.

After Seeing the Fourth Exhibition of the West Lake Art Academy

— Zhang Tianyi

After the Fourth Exhibition of the West Lake Art Academy, I really wanted to say a few words, although many people have already published some critical articles in the newspapers. I am not just joining in the fun. It's just that after visiting this art exhibition, I felt a sense of relief, and therefore I couldn't help but express my feelings.

I believe that at a time when so-called post-impressionist "art disciples are all over the world," the West Lake Art Academy's opening of this exhibition is a very interesting and meaningful thing.

Last year, we saw a solo exhibition belonging to a post-impressionist. We only saw him frantically applying some paint, and gained nothing else. This is not surprising, as this is the style of the school, as long as the paint is applied vigorously, the outline doesn't matter. But the paintings of the West Lake Art Academy are very powerful in their expression of lines. Lines are originally very troublesome, so this kind of painting art, which has reached its late stage, can only enjoy itself in the paint. The powerful lines symbolize the art that is rising. Although the styles of this art exhibition are different, they are consistent in this point.

The so-called enjoying oneself in the paint, if it is said that color represents emotion, and therefore piling up red and green masses is a strong emotion, this is an exaggeration. Neglecting lines and only brushing paint, this kind of painting method is easy to imitate. The Chinese followers of Cézanne only returned to this "sect" for the sake of convenient imitation: imitation is the entire life of their works. But the people at the West Lake Art Academy just don't imitate, whether it's Chinese painting or Western painting. As soon as you see it, it makes you feel relieved and able to breathe freely. But if you say that this one is influenced by someone, and that one is influenced by someone, that's possible. But it's just influence, and the things are still the author's own.

As for the content, this art exhibition should also arouse attention. From the previous groping for personal desires (such as "Groping") and personal desires (such as "Desire for Life"), it has now developed to a broader aspect—like Bin Hong's "Alley Elegy," which is not just personal grief. Facing this painting, with Bin Hong's powerful lines and the placement of warm and cold colors, everyone will have a strong and profound impression.

In this time when content is not needed, lines are neglected, and only tricks are played with profits, creating a chaotic atmosphere, the West Lake Art Academy used a new posture to open this exhibition, which is a very pleasant thing. Even from the perspective of the artist's attitude, the teachers and students of the West Lake Art Academy are different from those loud-mouthed philistine artists. They don't flatter, don't ask great figures to write inscriptions, and don't add any badges to themselves. They just silently work hard to learn and practice. They are very humble, and they have never been complacent. And they have achieved this result.

Two Folk Love Songs from Anhui

— Rui Zi

(1)

Seventeen or eighteen, a flower on a branch, if I don't look for my love now, when will I? Bamboo shoots grow old joint by joint, frost hits the leaves and they gradually wither, gradually wither, without my love, I suffer loneliness night after night.

(2)

Big stars in the sky face small stars, an eighteen-year-old sister has been looking for her love until now; I don't know how many dark night roads I have walked, I don't know how much fear and shock I have suffered, standing, I'm afraid of being seen, squatting, I'm afraid of mosquito bites, walking to the front village, the dogs bark, walking to the back village, the tigers hum. I have to summon up my courage and look forward, calling my love's name and scolding at the same time.

Random Notes

— Xia Chang

(12)

The short writings of the ancients often contain excellent works. For example, Zhang Yi (Baiyun) said to the monk Chuyun: "Continuous rain for ten days, moss encroaching on the stove's edge, no smoke in the morning chimney. Sitting quietly for a few breaths, I happily recite: 'Placing this body in the midst of ten thousand green shades, being poor with nine meals in thirty days is not poverty, if I could abstain from grains and fly lightly, who would be the host and guest of famous mountains?' I present this to my teacher, asking for a turning word." This is truly a person who can be said to be poor but successful. Also, Xu Fang said to Chen Gongzou: "Continuous rain is already annoying, especially for a lonely guest in an empty mountain? If I don't take a trip to the stream temple, this year's spring scenery will be entrusted to the flowing water again. A small banquet at Chang'an is very good, and seeking elsewhere may not be better. So it is advisable to stay here for a short time and choose good things to follow, without being hasty." This is also very unrestrained and evocative, making people think of pastoral life. As for what Luo Shizhen (Yixian) said to Tan Shaocheng: "Sublime interest enters my heart, forgetting that the pots and kettles are all empty," this is all about the lack of poor people, and nature helps them, not only helping them to succeed, but also using nature as a painted cake to fill their hunger.

Dusk (6)

— Jin Yi

Qingsong slowly stood up from her seat and walked to Qingzhi's side, gently taking the flute from her; at this time, Qingzhi stared at her in astonishment with tear-filled eyes, as if asking why she was doing this.

Qingsong already understood her question, she said:

"Sister, I'm just afraid you'll be sad. Playing the flute is originally a tiring thing, and if you cry again, wouldn't that be too bad for your health?"

As she spoke, Qingsong used her handkerchief to wipe the tears from Qingzhi's face, but when Qingsong also sat down, they suddenly hugged each other and cried.

Dusk seemed to be gradually falling, the azure autumn sky became deep purple, then deep gray, and flocks of crows flew past in the sky. This easily made people think of this ancient city, whose rise and fall were all in the sounds of crows calling. Or it was a premonition that this city, this city was about to sink deeply into the darkness of night. In this declining scene, the autumn wind was still rolling up pieces of falling leaves, hitting the window, and uttering complaints that were not understood. They had had good times, and knowing that they would perish with the times, they turned themselves red and beautiful with a little energy; but as the days of autumn triumphantly advanced, they fell from above, and they were to be trampled by the feet of people and beasts, and become dust on the roadside. But the vast twilight could envelop everything, with neither beauty nor ugliness, making people forget everything and only become blurred shadows.

In the twilight scene, looking at the outline of them embracing, it was as if old lovers who had long lost the fire of youth, only weakly, like enduring lifelong suffering until they had white hair, met, the long and distant sad days made them have endless grievances to pour out; but also only weakly, like two withered vines intertwined, their bodies shaking as they embraced.

They both felt their heads spinning, and Qingsong gently opened the window. They leaned on each other and looked out the window, watching aimlessly, as if gaining a sense of emptiness and vastness. In this silence, they deeply felt a little bit of comfort for their bodies and minds.

Dinner was brought up by the maid, and they had to turn on the lights, and for a moment their eyes felt a strong stinging pain. But they gradually didn't feel anything, but after dinner, waiting for the maid to take the dishes away, they turned off the lights again and sat by the window; the beautiful autumn moon, big and round, rose up again.
